Fifth Shia Objection: Possibility of Imamate Vacuum
Sanusi presents and refutes the fifth Shia objection about imamate vacuum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Shia objection regarding the possibility of a vacuum in imamate under the election theory and how it is refuted by the possibility of appointment when no imam is known and by using preponderance.

Core Idea
Simultaneous elections do not leave the ummah without an imam; preponderance can resolve ambiguity.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a sophisticated Shia objection that aims to show the impossibility of election (ikhtiyar) as a method for appointing an imam. The objection argues that if two groups simultaneously elect different candidates, the ummah might be left without a valid imam. The refutation counters that an imam can be appointed when no imam is known, and that criteria exist to determine preponderance. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: first the objection, then the refutation.
The passage begins with 'Fifth: that the statement of choice...'
2
Analyze the objection's logical steps
Identify the scenario (two towns electing) and the three impossibilities that result (cannot judge both valid, both invalid, or identify the correct one). Then note the consequence: no new imam can be appointed.
The objection uses the possibility of simultaneity (muqarana) and precedence (sabq) as obstacles.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation makes two points: (1) An imam can be appointed when there is no known imam, and (2) preponderance (tarjih) can be used to determine the stronger candidate based on Shari'ah criteria.
The refutation does not specify which criteria but alludes to general principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس - أن القول بالاختيار يؤدي إلى خلو الزمان عن الإمام، وهو باطل بالاتفاق، وذلك فيما إذا عقد أهل بلدتين لمستعدين، ولم يعلم السبق. فإنه لا يمكن الحكم بصحتهما لاحتمال المقارنة ولا بفسادهما لاحتمال السبق ، ولا بتعين الصحيح لعدم الوقوف، وحينئذ لا يمكن نصب إمام آخر لاحتمال كونه ثانياً، ورد بأنه ينصب إمام بعدم العلم بوجود الإمام على أنه يمكن الترجيح بجهاته .
Fifth: that the statement of choice (ikhtiyar) leads to a period being empty of an imam, which is invalid by agreement. This occurs when the people of two towns pledge allegiance to two candidates, and precedence (sabq) is not known. For it is not possible to judge both as valid due to possible simultaneity, nor both as invalid due to possible precedence, nor to identify the correct one due to lack of knowledge. Then, no other imam can be appointed because he might be a second. It is refuted by saying that an imam is appointed only when there is no knowledge of the existence of an imam, and it is possible to give preponderance (tarjih) by its aspects.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth Shia objection and its refutation. The objection argues that election can lead to a period without an imam if two groups in different towns each elect a candidate and the precedence (sabq) of one over the other is unknown. In that case, one cannot confirm either as valid because they might have been simultaneous, nor reject both because one might have preceded, nor determine the correct one due to lack of evidence. Consequently, no new imam can be appointed since that would risk having two imams. The refutation states that an imam can be appointed when there is no known imam, and that the problem of precedence can be resolved by using the known aspects of preponderance (tarijih) from the Shari'ah (like virtue, precedence in Islam, etc.). Therefore, the objection does not establish an impossibility.

Key Terms
السبق
التقارن
الترجيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The refutation claims that there is a specific procedure in the Shari'ah for choosing between simultaneous candidates.
Correction: The refutation does not specify a procedure; it only states that preponderance by its aspects is possible, implying that reasonable criteria can be used.

Checkpoint
What is the refutation to the objection that simultaneous elections might leave the ummah without an imam?
A) The objection is impossible because elections cannot occur simultaneously
B) An imam is appointed when there is no known imam, and preponderance (tarjih) can be used
C) The Prophet left a rule for such cases
D) Both elections are invalid

Key Takeaway
The objection fails because the community can appoint an imam using established criteria when no imam is known.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a choice between two seemingly good options and no clear answer, do you actively seek out the criteria of preponderance (tarjih) that Allah has provided, or do you remain stuck, afraid to act? Which of your own decisions have been paralyzed by the fear of making a mistake, and how might this lesson's method of tarjih free you to move forward?
?
The Shia objection assumes that uncertainty about leadership necessarily leads to chaos. In your own life, when you lack clear external guidance (from parents, scholars, or leaders), do you trust that Allah has left you a way to discern the best path, or do you default to inaction and blame the lack of direction? What if the very ambiguity is meant to push you to use the tools He gave you?
?
This passage shows that even in a complex situation, Islam does not leave the community without a means to resolve it. Where in your life have you wrongly assumed that because a matter is complicated, you are excused from taking a stand or making a decision? Will you commit to using the criteria of tarjih—like priority, virtue, and benefit—in your next difficult choice, no matter how uncertain it feels?

The Sixth Shia Objection: Prophet's Practice and Succession
Refutes the claim that the Prophet always appointed deputies, so he must have done so for his succession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Shia argument that the Prophet's practice of appointing deputies and giving clear explanations necessarily implies he appointed a successor for the imamate.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice does not prove he must have appointed a successor – it's mere improbability.

This lesson examines the sixth and final Shia objection to the Sunni position on the caliphate. The objection argues from the Prophet's consistent behavior: he always appointed deputies for short trips and never failed to explain even the smallest religious matters. Therefore, the Shia claim, it is inconceivable that he would leave the most important matter – succession – unaddressed. The author counters that this is merely an argument from improbability, not logical necessity, and that the Sunni position is no less plausible than the Shia alternative.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage which presents the Shia argument. Note the examples given: appointing deputies for short absences, explaining even minor rulings like toilet etiquette.
The objection uses the Prophet's 'sira' (biography) as evidence.
2
Identify the refutation
Read the author's answer. Notice that he calls it 'mere improbability' (isti'bad) and then offers a parity argument: delegating to the community (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd) is no more improbable than delegating to an infallible group.
The refutation does not deny the facts; it challenges the inference.
3
Understand the logical structure
Recognize that the objection is based on a pattern of behavior, but the author points out that patterns do not necessitate a specific conclusion when alternative explanations exist.
This is a common dialectical move in kalam: showing that an argument is not decisive.
4
Reflect on the key terms
Consider the terms 'isti'bad' (improbability), 'ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd' (people of loosening and binding), and 'ta'ifat al-'isma' (group of infallibles). How do they frame the debate?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس - أن سيرة النبي وطريقته على أنه كان لا يترك الاستخلاف على المدينة وغيرها من البلاد في غيبه مدة قليلة، ولا البيان في أدنى ما يحتاج إليه من الفرائض والسنن والآداب حتى في أمر قضاء الحاجة ومسح ذلك، فكيف يترك الاستخلاف في غيبة الوفاة والبيان فيما هو أساس المهمات؟ والجواب أن ذلك مجرد استبعاد على أن التفويض إلى اختيار أهل الحل والعقد ليس بأبعد من التفويض إلى طائفة العصمة، ونحو ذلك.
Sixth: that the biography (sira) and way of the Prophet, peace be upon him, was that he would not leave out appointing a deputy over Medina and other towns during his absence for a short period, nor [would he leave out] explanation (bayan) in the least of what is needed of obligations, sunan, and manners, even in matters of relieving oneself and wiping [after toilet]. So how could he leave out appointment of a successor (istikhlaf) at the time of death and explanation of what is the basis of important matters? The answer is that this is mere improbability (isti'bad), and that delegating to the choice of the people of loosening and binding (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd) is not more improbable than delegating to a group of infallibles (ta'ifat al-'isma), and so on.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth and final Shia objection and its refutation. The objection argues from the Prophet's general practice: he used to appoint deputies (istikhlaf) even for short absences from Medina, and he never failed to give clear explanation (bayan) for the smallest religious obligations, including matters like relieving oneself. Therefore, it is inconceivable (isti'bad) that he would neglect to appoint a successor for his permanent absence (death) and to clarify what is the most fundamental matter (the imamate). The refutation dismisses this as mere 'improbability' (isti'bad), not a logical proof. Moreover, the author points out that delegating the choice to the community's electors (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd) is no less likely than delegating it to an infallible group (ta'ifat al-'isma) as the Shia claim. In other words, the argument from practice does not rule out the possibility that the Prophet intentionally left the matter to communal choice. Thus the objection is not decisive.

Key Terms
السيرة
الاستخلاف
البيان
الاستبعاد
أهل الحل والعقد
طائفة العصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the refutation denies that the Prophet appointed deputies or gave explanations. Actually, the author does not deny the facts; he questions the inference from those facts to the necessity of a designated successor.
Correction: The author accepts the Prophetic practice described but argues that it does not logically entail a specific succession arrangement; alternative arrangements are equally plausible.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the Shia argument that the Prophet always appointed deputies and gave clear rulings, so he must have done so for succession?
A) By denying that the Prophet appointed deputies
B) By calling it mere improbability and noting that delegation to the community is not less probable than delegation to an infallible group
C) By saying the Prophet did not care about the imamate
D) By claiming there was no need for a successor

Key Takeaway
The Shia argument from the Prophet's practice is refuted as an appeal to improbability, not a decisive proof, and the Sunni position is shown to be equally plausible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt certain about a religious belief simply because it seemed 'obvious' or 'likely'? Reflect on a specific conviction you hold. Is your certainty based on evidence or on mere improbability (isti'bad) that the opposite could be true? Commit to re-examining that conviction by directly consulting the sources.

Detailed Causes for Dissolution of the Imamate
The author enumerates specific causes that dissolve the imamate contract, following a general principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific causes that invalidate the imamate contract as enumerated by the author, including apostasy, mental incapacity, sensory loss, and voluntary resignation due to inability.

Core Idea
The imamate dissolves when its essential purpose can no longer be fulfilled.

In this passage, the author elaborates on the causes that dissolve the contract of imamate. He moves from a general principle—anything that vitiates the purpose of imamate—to a detailed list of specific conditions. These include apostasy, madness, captivity, and various physical or mental impairments that prevent the imam from fulfilling his duties.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on the enumeration of causes. Note the repeated 'كذا' and 'وكذا' which introduce each cause.
2
Identify the categories of causes
The causes fall into three broad categories: those involving loss of faith (apostasy), loss of mental capacity (madness, illness, forgetfulness), and loss of physical ability (blindness, deafness, muteness, captivity), as well as voluntary resignation due to inability.
Resignation due to inability is an act of the imam himself.
3
Connect to the general principle
Each cause listed ultimately removes the purpose of imamate. Reflect on how each cause prevents the imam from managing the affairs of Muslims.
This helps you see the systematic reasoning behind the list.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: خاتمة (عقد الإمامة ينحل بما يخل بمقصودها كالردة والجنون، وبعض الأمراض، وبخلعه نفسه بسبب وبالغلبة عليه إذا صار إماماً بالغلبة. واختلف في خلعه نفسه بلا سبب وفي انعزاله بالفسق. ينحل عقد الإمامة بما يزول به مقصود الإمامة كالردة والجنون المطبق وصيرورته أسيراً لا يرجى خلاصه، وكذا بالمرض الذي ينسيه العلوم وبالعمى، والصمم والخرس، وكذا بخلعه نفسه لعجزه عن القيام بمصالح المسلمين، وإن لم يكن ظاهراً، بل استشعره في نفسه. وعليه يحمل خلع الحسن (رضي الله تعالى عنه) نفسه. وأما خلعه لنفسه بلا سبب ففيه خلاف وكذا في انعزاله بالفسق. والأكثرون على أنه لا ينعزل. وهو المختار من مذهب الشافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه وأبي حنيفة، وعن محمد (رضي الله تعالى عنهما) روايتان. ويستحق العزل بالاتفاق. ومن صار إماماً بالقهر والغلبة ينعزل بأن يقهره آخر ويغلبه. وأما القاضي فينعزل بالفسق على الأظهر.
He said: Conclusion. The contract of imamate is dissolved by whatever vitiates its purpose, such as apostasy, madness, some illnesses, and his resignation of himself due to a reason, and by being overpowered if he became imam by overpowering. And there is disagreement concerning his resignation of himself without a cause and concerning his removal due to transgression. The contract of imamate is dissolved by whatever removes the purpose of imamate, such as apostasy, continuous madness, his becoming a captive from whose release there is no hope, likewise by an illness that causes forgetfulness of knowledge, and by blindness, deafness, and muteness, likewise by his resignation of himself due to his inability to manage the interests of the Muslims, even if it is not apparent, but he perceives it in himself. And upon this is based the resignation of al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) of himself. As for his resignation of himself without a cause, there is disagreement concerning it, and likewise concerning his removal due to transgression. The majority hold that he is not removed. And that is the chosen view in the school of al-Shāfiʿī (may Allah be pleased with him) and Abū Ḥanīfa, and from Muḥammad (may Allah be pleased with them both) there are two narrations. And he deserves removal by consensus. And whoever becomes imam by force and overpowering is removed by being overpowered by another. And as for the judge, he is removed due to transgression on the most apparent view.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion (khātima) that lists the causes for the dissolution of the contract of imamate. The author first gives a brief summary: the imamate contract is dissolved by anything that destroys its purpose, such as apostasy, madness, some illnesses, resignation for a valid reason, and being overpowered if the imam gained power through overpowering. He notes disagreement on resignation without cause and removal due to transgression. Then he elaborates: dissolution occurs due to apostasy, continuous madness, hopeless captivity, illness causing forgetfulness, blindness, deafness, muteness, and resignation due to inability to manage Muslim interests (even if only perceived internally). He gives the example of al-Hasan's resignation. He then discusses the disagreement: the majority holds that resignation without cause does not remove the imam, and similarly transgression does not remove him (this is the chosen view in the Shāfiʿī and Ḥanafī schools, with a differing narration from Muḥammad). However, removal (ʿazl) is deserved by consensus. For an imam who came to power through force, he is removed when another overpowers him. As for a judge (qāḍī), he is removed due to transgression on the most apparent view.

عمى
صمم
خرس

Checkpoint
Which of the following is explicitly mentioned as a cause for dissolution of the imamate contract in this passage?
A) Old age
B) Continuous madness
C) Financial insolvency
D) Disagreement with advisors

Key Takeaway
The imamate contract dissolves when the imam loses the capacity to fulfill its core purpose, whether due to apostasy, mental incapacity, sensory loss, or voluntary resignation due to inability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you hold any position of responsibility, are you truly fulfilling its purpose, or are you clinging to it out of pride? Would you have the courage to step down, like al-Hasan, upon perceiving your own inability, even if others do not see it?
?
This lesson teaches that the imamate dissolves when its purpose can no longer be met. What roles in your life—parent, teacher, friend—might you be holding onto despite no longer serving their real purpose? What is preventing you from letting go?
?
The list includes sensory and mental incapacities that disqualify a leader. Are you developing the inner and outer capacities needed for the responsibilities Allah has given you, or are you neglecting them while hoping others don't notice?

Disagreements on Dissolution: Resignation Without Cause and Transgression
The author discusses disputed causes of dissolution and special cases for imams by force and judges.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement regarding whether an imam can resign without cause and whether he is removed due to transgression, as well as the special cases of an imam by force and a judge.

Core Idea
Not every act of resignation or transgression dissolves the imamate; the majority holds the imam remains.

The author now turns to disputed cases. Having listed clear causes, he addresses two scenarios: an imam who resigns without any apparent reason, and an imam who commits transgression (fisq). The majority of scholars, including the founders of the Shāfiʿī and Ḥanafī schools, hold that such an imam is not automatically removed. However, a judge is removed by fisq on the strongest view. Additionally, an imam who gained power through force is removed when another overpowers him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage noting the two points of disagreement: resignation without cause and removal due to fisq. Also note the separate rulings for an imam by force and for a judge.
2
Identify the two disputed issues
The first is resignation without any legitimate reason. The second is whether transgression (fisq) causes removal. Note the majority view and the chosen madhhab positions.
The author mentions that removal (ʿazl) is deserved by consensus, meaning the imam deserves to be removed, but the contract is not automatically dissolved.
3
Contrast the case of the judge
Unlike the imam, the judge is removed due to fisq on the most apparent view. Consider why the judge's position might be more susceptible to removal.
4
Understand the case of the imam by force
An imam who came to power through overpowering (qahr wa ghalaba) is removed when another overpowers him. This is a different rule because his authority is based on force.
This acknowledges political realities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage is a conclusion (khātima) that lists the causes for the dissolution of the contract of imamate. The author first gives a brief summary: the imamate contract is dissolved by anything that destroys its purpose, such as apostasy, madness, some illnesses, resignation for a valid reason, and being overpowered if the imam gained power through overpowering. Key Takeaway
The imam is not automatically removed by resignation without cause or by transgression, though he deserves removal by consensus; judges are removed by fisq, and usurpers are removed by being overpowered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Reflect on a time when you witnessed a leader or person in authority committing an act of transgression. How did you react? Did you assume their authority was automatically stripped, or did you struggle with the tension between their sin and their responsibility? What does this lesson teach you about that situation?
?
The judge is removed by transgression, but the imam is not. What does this distinction reveal about the different levels of responsibility and accountability? When you are in a position of leadership, do you hold yourself to the higher standard? Or do you rely on the leniency given to leaders to avoid consequences?

The Refutation of Explicit Appointment – First Argument
The author presents the first argument: if explicit appointment existed, it would be known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument against the claim of an explicit appointment of Ali, based on the behavior of the senior Companions.

Core Idea
If an explicit text existed, the Companions would have known and followed it.

The author begins his refutation by stating the positions of different groups. He then presents a powerful argument: if the Prophet had explicitly appointed Ali, such a crucial matter would have been widely known. The senior Companions, who were closest to the Prophet, would not have hesitated or disagreed at the Saqifa gathering. In this lesson, we examine this logical argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the author's presentation of the different claims.
Notice the categories: majority, some, Shia, Imamiyya.
2
Identify the logical premise
Recognize the key premise: an explicit text in a great matter would be widely known and accepted.
3
Consider the counter-claim
The author addresses the Shia claim that the Companions concealed the text out of envy. Understand why he considers this slander.
Think about the high character of the Companions mentioned.
4
Reflect on the strength
Think about why the author finds this argument compelling based on the character of the Companions and the historical context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الرابع - الجمهور على أنه ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) لم ينص على إمام . وقيل : نص على أبي بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه نصاً خفياً . وقيل : جلياً. وقالت الشيعة على علي كرم الله وجهه خفياً. والإمامية منهم : جلياً ايضاً ورد بوجهين : الأول - لو كان نص جلي في مثل هذا الأمر العلي لاشتهر وظهر على أجلة الصحابة الذين لهم زيادة قرب واختصاص بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) فلم يتوقفوا عن الإذعان ، ولم يترددوا حين اجتمعوا لهذا الشأن. ولم يختلفوا في التعيين، ولم يشكوا في الحق اليقين . والقول بأنهم كتموه بغضاً وحسداً، أو عناداً ولدداً، أو اعتقاداً لنسخه حين لم يعمل المحقون على دفعه، ولم يتمسك به المستحق لإثبات حقه افتراء و اجتراء وطعن في عظماء الأحياء ، بل في خير الأنبياء، بل في الكتاب الناطق لهم بالثناء. والعاقل المنصف لا يظن بجماعة وصفهم الله تعالى بكونهم خير الأمم و اتخذهم النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أمناء شريعة، وهداة طريقة مع علمه بحالهم ومالهم، واشتهر عدلهم وهداهم وتركهم هوا هم، وبذلهم الأموال والأنفس في محبته، وقتلهم الأقارب والعشائر لنصرته، و اتباع شريعته أنهم خالفوه قبل أن يدفنوه ، وعدلوا عن الحق، وخذلوه ، ونصر واعلى الباطل وأيدوه ، ومنعوا المستحق حقه وكتموه، ولم يقم هو بإظهاره وإعلانه مع علو شأنه وكثرة أعوانه كما قام به من غير تبعية حين أفضى الأمر إليه، وأقام الحجة والبرهان والسيف والسنان عليه. مع أن الخطب إذ ذاك أشد، والخصم ألد ، والمخالف لا يحويه الحد، ولا يحصيه العد. الثاني - أمارات ربما يفيد باجتماعها القطع بعدم النص، كقول العباس لعلي وعمر لأبي عبيدة : امدد يدك أبايعك، وقول أبي بكر : بايعوا عمر أو أبا عبيدة.
He said: The Fourth Investigation – The majority hold that he (peace be upon him) did not explicitly appoint an imam. And it was said: He implicitly appointed Abū Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him). And it was said: explicitly. The Shīʿa said: (he appointed) ʿAlī (may Allah honor his face) implicitly. And the Imāmiyya among them said: explicitly as well. He refuted it with two points: The first – if there had been an explicit text concerning such a great matter, it would have become widespread and manifest to the eminent Companions who had extra closeness and special relation to the Prophet (peace be upon him), so they would not have hesitated to submit, nor would they have delayed when they gathered for this matter, nor would they have disagreed about the designation, nor would they have doubted the certain truth. And the claim that they concealed it out of hatred and envy, or stubbornness and hostility, or belief in its abrogation when the rightful ones did not act to defend it and the one entitled did not cling to it to establish his right, is slander and insolence and an attack on the great living persons, rather on the best of prophets, rather on the Book that speaks in their praise. The rational and fair person does not suspect a group whom Allah Almighty has described as being the best of nations, and whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) took as trustees of the Shariʿa and guides of the path, knowing their condition and what they had, and whose justice and guidance were famous, and who abandoned their whims, and spent wealth and lives in his love, and killed relatives and clans for his victory and following his Shariʿa – that they opposed him before they buried him, deviated from the truth, abandoned him, supported and elevated falsehood, prevented the one entitled from his right and concealed it, while he (the Prophet) did not manifest it and proclaim it despite his high status and many supporters, as he did without any follower when the matter came to him, and he established proof, argument, sword, and spear against it, even though the situation at that time was more severe, the opponent more stubborn, and the dissenter was not contained by bounds nor counted by numbers. The second – indications that perhaps together yield certainty of the absence of explicit text, such as the saying of al-ʿAbbās to ʿAlī and ʿUmar to Abū ʿUbayda: 'Extend your hand so that I may pledge allegiance to you,' and the saying of Abū Bakr: 'Pledge allegiance to ʿUmar or Abū ʿUbayda.'
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is the fourth investigation (al-mabḥath al-rābiʿ) concerning whether the Prophet explicitly appointed a successor. The author states the positions: the majority say no explicit text (naṣṣ), some say a hidden text for Abū Bakr, some say explicit, the Shīʿa say hidden text for ʿAlī, the Imāmiyya say explicit text for ʿAlī. He refutes with two arguments. The first argument: if there were an explicit text for such an important matter, it would have been widely known and accepted by the senior Companions, who were closest to the Prophet. They would not have delayed or disagreed at the Saqīfa gathering. The claim that they concealed it out of envy or other motives is slander against them. The author emphasizes that these Companions are praised by Allah and the Prophet, and it is inconceivable that they would oppose the Prophet immediately after his death. The second argument: circumstantial evidence from statements at the Saqīfa, such as al-ʿAbbās offering to pledge to ʿAlī, ʿUmar to Abū ʿUbayda, and Abū Bakr suggesting ʿUmar or Abū ʿUbayda, which indicate the absence of a definitive appointment.

Key Terms
نص
جلياً
خفياً
الشيعة
الإمامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shia claim that the Prophet made an implicit appointment of Ali that was only known to a few.
Correction: The author argues that such an important matter would have been known and accepted by all senior Companions, and they would not have acted as they did at Saqifa.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument the author uses to refute the claim of an explicit text (nass jali) appointing Ali?
A) The Shia themselves disagree about the type of text.
B) If such a text existed, it would have been widely known and the Companions would not have disagreed.
C) The Prophet explicitly said he would not appoint a successor.
D) Ali himself denied any appointment.

Key Takeaway
The first argument establishes that an explicit appointment would have been universally known and accepted, so its absence proves no such appointment existed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author argues that if the Prophet had appointed ʿAlī explicitly, he would have made it public despite opposition. Are you willing to publicly affirm a truth you believe in, even if it brings you into conflict with your community or family? What holds you back?
?
The Companions are described as sacrificing relatives and wealth for the Prophet's sake. Do you have that level of loyalty to the truth? When was the last time you chose truth over personal comfort or relationship?
?
Imagine you were at the Saqifa. The evidence for an explicit text is absent, but your heart inclines toward a certain person. Would you submit to the lack of evidence and accept the consensus, or would you insist on your own wish? Examine your attachment to your own opinions.

The Refutation of Explicit Appointment – Second Argument
The author presents the second argument: indications from Saqifa prove no explicit text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against the claim of an explicit appointment of Ali, based on circumstantial evidence from the Saqifa gathering.

Core Idea
Statements at Saqifa indicate no one knew of an appointment.

The author gives a second, more concise argument: circumstantial evidence from the events at Saqifa contradicts the existence of an explicit text. He cites statements by al-Abbas, Umar, and Abu Bakr that show they were unaware of any appointment. In this lesson, we examine this argument and its evidentiary value.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the short Arabic passage for the second argument and note the examples the author provides.
The argument is based on what was said at Saqifa.
2
Understand the inference
Why does the author believe these statements prove there was no explicit text? Think about what they imply about the knowledge of the Companions.
3
Evaluate the strength
Consider how this argument complements the first logical argument. Together they form a cumulative case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الرابع - الجمهور على أنه ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) لم ينص على إمام . وقيل : نص على أبي بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه نصاً خفياً . وقيل : جلياً. وقالت الشيعة على علي كرم الله وجهه خفياً. والإمامية منهم : جلياً ايضاً ورد بوجهين : الأول - لو كان نص جلي في مثل هذا الأمر العلي لاشتهر وظهر على أجلة الصحابة الذين لهم زيادة قرب واختصاص بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) فلم يتوقفوا عن الإذعان ، ولم يترددوا حين اجتمعوا لهذا الشأن. ولم يختلفوا في التعيين، ولم يشكوا في الحق اليقين . والقول بأنهم كتموه بغضاً وحسداً، أو عناداً ولدداً، أو اعتقاداً لنسخه حين لم يعمل المحقون على دفعه، ولم يتمسك به المستحق لإثبات حقه افتراء و اجتراء وطعن في عظماء الأحياء ، بل في خير الأنبياء، بل في الكتاب الناطق لهم بالثناء. والعاقل المنصف لا يظن بجماعة وصفهم الله تعالى بكونهم خير الأمم و اتخذهم النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أمناء شريعة، وهداة طريقة مع علمه بحالهم ومالهم، واشتهر عدلهم وهداهم وتركهم هوا هم، وبذلهم الأموال والأنفس في محبته، وقتلهم الأقارب والعشائر لنصرته، و اتباع شريعته أنهم خالفوه قبل أن يدفنوه ، وعدلوا عن الحق، وخذلوه ، ونصر واعلى الباطل وأيدوه ، ومنعوا المستحق حقه وكتموه، ولم يقم هو بإظهاره وإعلانه مع علو شأنه وكثرة أعوانه كما قام به من غير تبعية حين أفضى الأمر إليه، وأقام الحجة والبرهان والسيف والسنان عليه. مع أن الخطب إذ ذاك أشد، والخصم ألد ، والمخالف لا يحويه الحد، ولا يحصيه العد. الثاني - أمارات ربما يفيد باجتماعها القطع بعدم النص، كقول العباس لعلي وعمر لأبي عبيدة : امدد يدك أبايعك، وقول أبي بكر : بايعوا عمر أو أبا عبيدة.
He said: The Fourth Investigation – The majority hold that he (peace be upon him) did not explicitly appoint an imam. And it was said: He implicitly appointed Abū Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him). And it was said: explicitly. The Shīʿa said: (he appointed) ʿAlī (may Allah honor his face) implicitly. And the Imāmiyya among them said: explicitly as well. He refuted it with two points: The first – if there had been an explicit text concerning such a great matter, it would have become widespread and manifest to the eminent Companions who had extra closeness and special relation to the Prophet (peace be upon him), so they would not have hesitated to submit, nor would they have delayed when they gathered for this matter, nor would they have disagreed about the designation, nor would they have doubted the certain truth. And the claim that they concealed it out of hatred and envy, or stubbornness and hostility, or belief in its abrogation when the rightful ones did not act to defend it and the one entitled did not cling to it to establish his right, is slander and insolence and an attack on the great living persons, rather on the best of prophets, rather on the Book that speaks in their praise. The rational and fair person does not suspect a group whom Allah Almighty has described as being the best of nations, and whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) took as trustees of the Shariʿa and guides of the path, knowing their condition and what they had, and whose justice and guidance were famous, and who abandoned their whims, and spent wealth and lives in his love, and killed relatives and clans for his victory and following his Shariʿa – that they opposed him before they buried him, deviated from the truth, abandoned him, supported and elevated falsehood, prevented the one entitled from his right and concealed it, while he (the Prophet) did not manifest it and proclaim it despite his high status and many supporters, as he did without any follower when the matter came to him, and he established proof, argument, sword, and spear against it, even though the situation at that time was more severe, the opponent more stubborn, and the dissenter was not contained by bounds nor counted by numbers. The second – indications that perhaps together yield certainty of the absence of explicit text, such as the saying of al-ʿAbbās to ʿAlī and ʿUmar to Abū ʿUbayda: 'Extend your hand so that I may pledge allegiance to you,' and the saying of Abū Bakr: 'Pledge allegiance to ʿUmar or Abū ʿUbayda.'
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is the fourth investigation (al-mabḥath al-rābiʿ) concerning whether the Prophet explicitly appointed a successor. The author states the positions: the majority say no explicit text (naṣṣ), some say a hidden text for Abū Bakr, some say explicit, the Shīʿa say hidden text for ʿAlī, the Imāmiyya say explicit text for ʿAlī. He refutes with two arguments. The first argument: if there were an explicit text for such an important matter, it would have been widely known and accepted by the senior Companions, who were closest to the Prophet. They would not have delayed or disagreed at the Saqīfa gathering. The claim that they concealed it out of envy or other motives is slander against them. The author emphasizes that these Companions are praised by Allah and the Prophet, and it is inconceivable that they would oppose the Prophet immediately after his death. The second argument: circumstantial evidence from statements at the Saqīfa, such as al-ʿAbbās offering to pledge to ʿAlī, ʿUmar to Abū ʿUbayda, and Abū Bakr suggesting ʿUmar or Abū ʿUbayda, which indicate the absence of a definitive appointment.

Key Terms
نص
أمارات
سقيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Saqifa gathering was a usurpation of Ali's rights despite an explicit text.
Correction: The author argues that the statements made at Saqifa by key figures show they had no knowledge of any such text, thereby disproving its existence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example the author uses to support the second argument?
A) The Prophet's hadith on the caliphate.
B) Ali's silence after Saqifa.
C) Al-Abbas offering to pledge allegiance to Ali.
D) The Battle of Jamal.

Key Takeaway
The second argument uses circumstantial evidence from Saqifa to demonstrate that the Companions acted as if no explicit appointment existed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held onto a belief about someone's authority that was contradicted by their own actions? The Companions at Saqifa acted as if no appointment existed. Are you willing to let go of assumptions when the evidence undermines them?
?
The Companions did not claim a divine appointment for themselves. Do you ever assert certainty from God about matters where He has given no clear directive? How can you guard against claiming 'nass' where there is none?
?
If you were faced with a decision where the evidence suggested no clear divine instruction, would you humbly consult others like the Companions did, or insist on a hidden text? What would that reveal about your trust in God's guidance versus your own desires?

Views on the Prophet's Appointment of a Successor
The author enumerates the views on whether the Prophet explicitly or implicitly appointed an Imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing classical positions on whether the Prophet (SAW) explicitly designated a successor (Imam) and the key terminology used in these debates.

Core Idea
The majority held the Prophet left no explicit appointment; other groups claimed implicit or explicit texts for Abu Bakr or Ali.

This passage introduces one of the most contested issues in Islamic political theology: did the Prophet designate a successor? The author presents the spectrum of views—from the majority who deny any explicit text, to Shia claims of an implicit or explicit text for Ali. Understanding these positions is essential for grasping later theological arguments about the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style: each view is stated in a short phrase.
2
Identify the four positions
The passage presents two main categories: the majority view (no text), and those who claim a text. Among the latter, there are sub-views: some say implicit text for Abu Bakr, others explicit; the Shia say implicit for Ali, the Imamiyya explicit.
Use the key terms 'نص جلي' and 'نص خفي' to distinguish explicit vs implicit.
3
Understand the refutation setup
The passage ends with 'ورد بوجهين' (and it is refuted in two ways). This signals that the author will now argue against these claims. Be ready to evaluate the arguments in the next lesson.
This is a classic kalam structure: state the views, then refute them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الرابع - الجمهور على أنه (صلى الله عليه وسلم ) لم ينص على إمام . وقيل : نص على أبي بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه نصاً خفياً . وقيل : جلياً. وقالت الشيعة على علي كرم الله وجهه) خفياً. والإمامية منهم : جلياً ايضاً ورد بوجهين :
He said: The fourth section - The majority are of the view that he (peace be upon him) did not explicitly designate an Imam. And it was said: he explicitly designated Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, with an implicit text. And it was said: with an explicit text. And the Shia said: he explicitly designated Ali, may God honor his face, with an implicit text. And the Imamiyya among them: with an explicit text as well. And it is refuted in two ways:
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the different positions regarding whether the Prophet (SAW) explicitly designated a successor (imam). The author first states the majority view that there was no explicit text (nass) designating anyone. Then he mentions views that there was an implicit text (nass khafiyy) for Abu Bakr, and another view that it was explicit and clear (nass jaliyy). The Shia are reported to hold that there was an implicit text for Ali, while the Imamiyya subgroup asserts an explicit text. The author then introduces that these claims are refuted in two ways, setting up the following arguments.

Correction: The passage says the majority did not explicitly designate an Imam (لم ينص على إمام). This does not rule out an implicit reference, but the majority view is that there was no formal text.

Key Takeaway
The classical dispute over the Prophet's appointment of a successor centers on whether there was any explicit or implicit text designating someone, with the majority holding that no such text exists.

?

?

?
If there were indeed an implicit text for Abu Bakr or Ali, would you be willing to follow it even if it challenged your current loyalties? Examine your attachment to the leader you support—is it based on truth or on habit?

The First Refutation: Impossibility of Concealing a Clear Text
Argument: a clear text would have been widely known and acted upon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that a clear text designating a successor would have necessarily become widely known, and why the suggestion of deliberate concealment is untenable.

Core Idea
If there was a clear text, it would have been known. The Companions' hesitation proves it didn't exist.

The debate over succession hinges on whether the Prophet explicitly appointed a successor. In this first refutation, the author argues from necessity: a clear text on such a vital matter would have been universally known among the Companions. Their subsequent actions—hesitation, discussion, and disagreement—demonstrate that no such text existed. This lesson unpacks that logical argument and addresses the counterclaim of deliberate concealment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the strong logical structure: 'if...then'. Let the argument sink in before analyzing.
Pay attention to the emotional tone when refuting the concealment claim.
2
Identify premise and necessary consequence
Identify the main premise (if a clear text existed) and its necessary consequence (it would be widely known and acted upon without hesitation).
3
Examine the refutation of concealment
The author rejects the idea that Companions concealed the text. List the motives he dismisses and his reasoning against them.
He uses strong language: 'slander and aggression and aspersion'.
4
Reflect on the argument's implications
Consider why this argument matters in the larger theological debate. How does it safeguard the integrity of the Companions?
This connects to the Sunni view of Companions' justice ('adala).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول - لو كان نص جلي في مثل هذا الأمر العلي لاشتهر وظهر على أجلة الصحابة الذين لهم زيادة قرب واختصاص بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) فلم يتوقفوا عن الإذعان ، ولم يترددوا حين اجتمعوا لهذا الشأن. ولم يختلفوا في التعيين، ولم يشكوا في الحق اليقين . والقول بأنهم كتموه بغضاً وحسداً، أو عناداً ولدداً، أو اعتقاداً لنسخه حين لم يعمل المحقون على دفعه، ولم يتمسك به المستحق لإثبات حقه افتراء و اجتراء وطعن في عظماء الأحياء ، بل في خير الأنبياء، بل في الكتاب الناطق لهم بالثناء. والعاقل المنصف لا يظن بجماعة وصفهم الله تعالى بكونهم خير الأمم) و اتخذهم النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أمناء شريعة، وهداة طريقة مع علمه بحالهم ومالهم، واشتهر عدلهم وهداهم وتركهم ،هواهم، وبذلهم الأموال والأنفس في محبته، وقتلهم الأقارب والعشائر النصرته، و اتباع شريعته (٢) أنهم خالفوه قبل أن يدفنوه ، وعدلوا عن الحق، وخذلوه ، ونصر واعلى الباطل وأيدوه ، ومنعوا المستحق حقه وكتموه، ولم يقم هو بإظهاره وإعلانه مع علو شأنه وكثرة أعوانه كما قام به من غير تبعية حين أفضى الأمر إليه، وأقام الحجة والبرهان والسيف والسنان عليه. مع أن الخطب إذ ذاك أشد، والخصم ألد ، والمخالف لا يحويه الحد، ولا يحصيه العد.
The first: If there had been a clear text in such a great matter, it would have become widely known and apparent to the senior Companions who had extra closeness and special connection to the Prophet (peace be upon him). Then they would not have hesitated to submit, nor would they have hesitated when they gathered for this affair. They would not have differed over the designation, nor doubted the certain truth. And the claim that they concealed it out of hatred and envy, or stubbornness and obstinacy, or belief in its abrogation — since those who were right did not act to advance it, nor did the one entitled cling to it to prove his right — is slander and aggression and aspersion upon the great ones of the living, indeed upon the best of prophets, indeed upon the speaking Book which praises them. A reasonable and fair person would not think of a group whom God Almighty described as 'the best of nations' and whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) took as trustees of the Sharia and guides of the way, while knowing their condition and what they possessed, and whose justice and guidance and abandonment of their desires became famous, and who sacrificed wealth and lives in his love, killed relatives and clans for his victory, and followed his Sharia — that they opposed him before they buried him, deviated from the truth, abandoned him, supported falsehood and aided it, prevented the rightful one from his right and concealed it, and that he himself did not manifest it and declare it despite his high rank and numerous supporters, as he did without any follower when the matter came to him, and he established the proof and demonstration and sword and spear against it. Moreover, the situation at that time was more severe, the opponent more obstinate, and the dissenter could not be contained by bounds nor counted by number.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This is a refutation (al-wajh al-awwal) against the claim that there was a clear explicit text designating a successor. The argument is: if such a text existed for such an important matter, it would have been widely known among the senior Companions, who were closest to the Prophet. They would not have hesitated or differed when they gathered to choose a leader after the Prophet's death. The opponents' suggestion that the Companions deliberately concealed the text out of hatred, envy, stubbornness, or belief in abrogation is rejected as slander. The author argues that it is inconceivable that the Companions, whom God praised as the best nation and whom the Prophet appointed as trustees of his religion, could have acted contrary to the truth immediately after his death. Moreover, if the rightful successor knew of such a text, he would have openly claimed his right, especially given the pressing circumstances. Thus, the absence of such widespread knowledge and action disproves the existence of a clear text.

Key Terms
نص جلي
الصحابة
الأئمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the Companions deliberately concealed a clear text designating Ali as successor due to envy or enmity.
Correction: The author argues this is slanderous and contradicts the known virtue of the Companions. If such a text existed, it would have been widely known, and the rightful successor would have asserted it.

Checkpoint
According to the first refutation, what would have necessarily happened if there had been a clear text appointing a successor?
A) The Companions would have concealed it out of envy.
B) It would have become widely known and the Companions would not have hesitated.
C) The successor would have remained silent.
D) The text would have been abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The logical necessity of widespread knowledge of a clear text, combined with the historical reality of Companions' hesitation, suffices to refute the existence of such a text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson argues that hesitation and disagreement prove a command was not clear. Where in your own life have you used 'lack of clarity' as an excuse for disobedience, when deep down you knew the truth? What would it cost you to admit that the hesitation is in you, not in the command?
?
The author calls the claim that the Companions concealed the truth 'slander against the best of prophets.' But you have likely hidden a truth from others to avoid conflict or embarrassment. When you conceal a truth you know, how are you any different from the accusation you reject? What would it take for you to openly declare that truth today?
?
Imagine standing before Allah with the excuse 'the truth was not clear to me.' This lesson shows that if the truth were truly unclear, there would be widespread confusion about it — but you see clear proofs everywhere. What truth are you avoiding because you prefer your own desires? What step will you take right now to submit to it without hesitation?

The Cumulative Indicators Against a Clear Text
The author lists multiple historical indicators that together disprove the existence of a clear text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a set of historical actions and statements from the early community collectively disprove the claim of an explicit textual designation for leadership.

Core Idea
Many signs, not one proof, together settle the matter.

This lesson presents the second refutation of the claim that there was a clear text (nass) appointing a specific successor. The author does not rely on a single argument but instead offers a collection of historical indicators (amarat) that, when combined, produce certainty that no such text existed. We will review these indicators and understand their cumulative force.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to familiarize yourself with the list of indicators. Notice the variety of sources: statements, actions, and silences.
2
Understand the cumulative method
Reflect on why none of these indicators alone might be conclusive, but together they create certainty. This is a key method in kalam: multiple independent pieces of evidence converging.
3
Identify each indicator
Go through the commentary and guided breakdown to list each indicator. Pay attention to the figures mentioned: al-Abbas, Umar, Abu Bakr, Ali, Talha, Muawiya, Zayd ibn Ali.
4
Consider the force of silence
One of the strongest indicators is the silence of Ali himself about any text in his sermons, letters, and boasts. Think about what that implies if a text existed.
5
Summarize the argument
In your own words, explain how the author uses these indicators to disprove the claim of a clear text. Write one paragraph.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - أمارات ربما يفيد باجتماعها القطع بعدم النص، كقول العباس لعلي وعمر لأبي عبيدة : امدد يدك أبايعك، وقول أبي بكر : بايعوا عمر أو أبا عبيدة. وقوله : وددت أني سألت النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) عن هذا الأمر فيمن هو . وكقبول علي الشورى وكقوله لطلحة : إن أردت بايعتك، وكاحتجاجه على معاوية بالبيعة له دون النص عليه . وكمعاضدته لأبي بكر وعمر في الأمور، وإشارته عليهما بما هو أصلح، وكسكوته عن النص عليه في خطبه وكتبه ومفاخراته، ومخاطباته. وكإنكار زيد ابن علي مع علو رتبته ذلك، وكذا كثير من عظماء أهل البيت.
The second: Indicators that perhaps, when combined, yield certainty about the absence of a text, such as the saying of al-Abbas to Ali and of Umar to Abu Ubayda: 'Extend your hand so that I may pledge allegiance to you,' and the saying of Abu Bakr: 'Pledge allegiance to Umar or Abu Ubayda.' And his saying: 'I wish I had asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about this matter to whom it belongs.' And Ali's acceptance of the shura (consultation) and his saying to Talha: 'If you wish, I will pledge allegiance to you.' And his argument against Muawiya based on the pledge of allegiance to himself, not on a text. And his support of Abu Bakr and Umar in affairs, and his advice to them on what was more appropriate. And his silence about a text in his sermons, letters, boasts, and addresses. And the denial of Zayd ibn Ali, despite his high rank, of that text. And likewise many of the great ones of the Ahl al-Bayt.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This is the second refutation, which presents a set of historical indicators (amarat) that collectively lead to the certainty that no clear text existed. The author provides examples: al-Abbas suggesting Ali or Umar suggesting Abu Ubayda for leadership; Abu Bakr suggesting Umar or Abu Ubayda; Abu Bakr's remark that he wished he had asked the Prophet to whom the matter belonged; Ali's acceptance of the consultative council (shura) and his offer to pledge allegiance to Talha; Ali arguing against Muawiya based on the pledge of allegiance to himself rather than a textual designation; Ali's cooperation with Abu Bakr and Umar and giving them advice; Ali's silence about any text in his sermons and correspondence; the denial of Zayd ibn Ali, despite being a prominent figure from the Ahl al-Bayt; and many others. These indicators, taken together, disprove the claim of an explicit text.

Key Terms
أمارات
القطع بعدم النص
الشورى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Each indicator alone is weak and therefore the argument fails.
Correction: The argument relies on the cumulative force of many independent indicators, which together produce certainty (qat') about the absence of a text.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is presented as an indicator that no clear text existed?
A) Ali refused to accept the shura.
B) Abu Bakr said he wished he had asked the Prophet about the matter.
C) Ali argued with Muawiya based on a clear text.
D) Zayd ibn Ali affirmed the existence of a text.

Key Takeaway
The absence of a clear text is known not from one proof but from a convergence of many historical facts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in Ali's position, knowing that many believed you should be the leader, would you have had the humility to support others and advise them? What does your answer reveal about your own attachment to status and authority? Will you cultivate that same humility today when others are given positions you feel you deserve?
?
The author says these indicators, when combined, produce certainty. In your own life, are you sometimes swayed by a single strong piece of evidence while ignoring the cumulative weight of many smaller signs? How can you train yourself to step back and see the bigger picture before forming a conviction? What might you be missing right now?
?
Zayd ibn Ali denied the text despite his high rank. Are there truths that you have been taught but have never sincerely questioned because of who taught them? Are you willing to follow evidence even if it means changing a long-held belief? Will you commit to investigating one such issue this week?

The Majority View and Alternative Claims of Explicit Designation
Enumeration of views on the designation of the successor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different positions on whether the Prophet explicitly designated a successor, including the majority view and the claims of implicit and explicit texts for Abu Bakr and Ali.

Core Idea
The majority held no explicit text; others claimed implicit or explicit texts for Abu Bakr or Ali.

Before examining the proofs, we need to map out the landscape of positions. The majority of scholars, including the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, held that the Prophet did not explicitly name a successor. However, various groups claimed there was either an implicit or explicit text for Abu Bakr or Ali. This passage enumerates those views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the majority view
First, notice that the majority (our companions, Mu'tazila, Khawarij) are mentioned as holding no explicit text.
2
Understand the implicit and explicit text for Abu Bakr
Al-Hasan al-Basri saw an implicit text in Abu Bakr leading prayer; some hadith scholars claimed an explicit text citing the inkpot and paper hadith.
3
Understand the Shia position for Ali
The Shia claimed an implicit text for Ali, and the Imamiyya claimed explicit texts citing several hadiths.
4
Note the agreement on implicit text
The passage notes that the implicit text (for Ali?) is agreed upon (by Shia), while explicit text is claimed only by Imamiyya, not Zaydiyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب جمهور أصحابنا والمعتزلة، والخوارج إلى ان النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) لم ينص على إمام بعده . وقيل : نص على أبي بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه فقال الحسن البصري: (۱) نصاً خفياً، وهو تقديمه إياه في الصلاة . وقال بعض أصحاب الحديث : نصاً جلياً، وهو ما روي أنه (عليه السلام) قال : ائتوني بدواة وقرطاس أكتب لأبي بكر كتاباً لا يختلف فيه اثنان ، ثم قال : يأبى الله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر (۲). وقيل : نصن على علي (رضي الله تعالى عنه . وهو مذهب الشيعة . أما النص الخفي، وهو الذي لا يعلم المراد منه بالضرورة فبالاتفاق، وأما النص الجلي فعند الإمامية دون الزيدية، وهو قوله : سلموا عليه بإمرة المؤمنين . وقوله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) مشيراً إليه وأخذاً بيده هذا خليفتي فيكم من بعدي، فاسمعوا له وأطيعوا وقوله (صلى الله عليه وسلم): أنت الخليفة من بعدي . وقوله () وقد جمع بني عبد المطلب : أيكم يبايعني ويؤازرني يكن أخي ووصيي وخليفتي من بعدي. فبايعه علي (رضي الله عنه) ثم استدل أهل الحق بطريقين: أحدهما ـ أنه لو كان نص جلي ظاهر المراد في مثل هذا الأمر الخطير المتعلق بمصالح الدين والدنيا لعامة الخلق لتواتر واشتهر فيما بين الصحابة ، وظهر على أجلتهم الذين لهم زيادة قرب بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) و اختصاص بهذا الأمر بحكم العادة. واللازم منتف . وإلا لم يتوقفوا عن الانقياد له والعمل بموجبه . ولم يترددوا حين اجتمعوا في سقيفة بني ساعدة لتعيين الأمام، ولم يقل الأنصار : ( منا أمير ومنكم أمير ولم تمل طائفة إلى أبي بكر (رضي الله عنه) وأخرى إلى علي رضي الله عنه وأخرى الى العباس
The majority of our companions, the Mu'tazila, and the Khawarij went to the view that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not explicitly designate an Imam after him. And it was said: he explicitly designated Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him. Al-Hasan al-Basri said: an implicit text, which is his giving him precedence in prayer. And some hadith scholars said: an explicit text, namely what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Bring me an inkpot and paper so that I may write for Abu Bakr a book concerning which two will not disagree,' then he said: 'God and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' And it was said: he explicitly designated Ali (may God be pleased with him). That is the doctrine of the Shia. As for the implicit text, which is not known necessarily, it is agreed upon; as for the explicit text, for the Imamiyya but not the Zaydiyya, it is his saying: 'Greet him with the title Commander of the Faithful,' and his saying (peace be upon him) pointing to him and taking his hand: 'This is my successor among you after me, so listen to him and obey,' and his saying (peace be upon him): 'You are the successor after me,' and his saying, when he gathered the Banu Abd al-Muttalib: 'Which of you will pledge allegiance to me and support me so that he may be my brother, my executor, and my successor after me?' So Ali (may God be pleased with him) pledged allegiance to him. Then the people of truth adduced two proofs: One of them — that if there had been a clear, explicit text on such a grave matter related to the religious and worldly interests of all people, it would have been transmitted successively and become famous among the Companions, and become apparent to the senior ones who had extra closeness to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and special connection to this matter by custom. And the consequent is false. Otherwise, they would not have hesitated to submit to it and act according to it. They would not have hesitated when they gathered in the portico of Banu Sa'ida to appoint the Imam, and the Ansar would not have said: 'An amir from us and an amir from you,' nor would one group have inclined to Abu Bakr (may God be pleased with him) and another to Ali (may God be pleased with him) and another to al-Abbas.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage restates the position of the majority (our companions, Mu'tazila, Khawarij) that the Prophet did not explicitly designate a successor. It then details the alternative views: some said there was an implicit text for Abu Bakr (his leading prayer), some hadith scholars claimed an explicit text (the hadith of the inkpot and paper and the statement 'God and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr'). The Shia claim an implicit text for Ali, and the Imamiyya claim an explicit text, citing several sayings of the Prophet. The author then presents the first proof (al-tariq al-awwal) of the people of truth: if there had been a clear, explicit text on such a crucial matter, it would have been transmitted widely (mutawatir) and famous among the Companions, especially the senior ones. The consequent is false, as seen in the events of Saqifa where there was hesitation, differences, and multiple candidates (Abu Bakr, Ali, al-Abbas). Therefore, no such clear text existed.

Key Terms
نص جلي
نص خفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The majority view is the same as the Shia view on no explicit text.
Correction: The majority holds no explicit text at all, while Shia claim explicit text for Ali.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group claimed an explicit text (nass jali) for Ali?
A) Majority
B) Some hadith scholars
C) Imamiyya
D) Zaydiyya

Key Takeaway
The passage presents a spectrum of views on whether the Prophet explicitly designated a successor, setting the stage for the rational proofs that follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage shows that early Muslims disagreed on whether the Prophet explicitly designated a successor. Do you personally accept any of these texts as binding? Which ones, and why? If you hold a view, have you ever tested it against the primary sources, or are you simply following your tradition?
?
The Shia claim explicit sayings from the Prophet designating Ali. If you are not Shia, how do you account for these narrations? Are you willing to examine them objectively, even if it challenges your current beliefs? What would it take to change your mind?
?
The Prophet's companions differed on this issue, yet they all loved him. How does this historical disagreement affect your confidence that the right caliph was chosen? Is it possible that both sides had valid evidence, and that sincerity matters more than being right? What does this teach you about handling disagreements among Muslims today?

The First Proof: No Explicit Text Because It Would Be Widely Transmitted
Presentation of the first proof (tariq awwal) against an explicit text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof against an explicit text: that if a clear text existed on such an important matter, it would have been transmitted widely and become famous, but it did not.

Core Idea
A clear text on a crucial matter would be mutawatir; its absence proves it never existed.

Having laid out the competing claims, the author now presents the first rational proof used by the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq). The proof is based on a logical conditional: if there had been a clear, explicit text on the succession, it would have been transmitted widely (tawatur) and become famous among the Companions, especially the senior ones. Since we do not see such widespread transmission, and in fact see hesitation and disagreement at Saqifa, the antecedent is false.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical conditional
The proof is based on 'if P then Q'. P = existence of a clear explicit text. Q = it would be mutawatir and famous.
2
Identify the consequent (Q)
The text says it would be transmitted successively, become famous, and be known to senior companions.
3
See the denial of the consequent
The consequent is false: we see no such widespread transmission, and the events of Saqifa show hesitation and disagreement.
4
Conclude the denial of the antecedent
Therefore, no clear explicit text existed.

Misconception & Correction

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what would have happened if a clear explicit text existed?
A) It would have been known only to a few.
B) It would have been forgotten.
C) It would have been transmitted widely and become famous.
D) It would have caused more disagreement.

Key Takeaway
The first proof uses the principle that a matter of such importance would have been transmitted widely, and the lack of such transmission disproves the existence of a clear explicit text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When facing a major decision in your life for which you cannot find an explicit text in the Quran or Sunnah, do you trust your God-given reason and the guidance of the community, or do you secretly expect a clear revelation that may never come? Are you willing to follow the example of the Companions who reasoned together without a text?
?
If you were among the Companions at Saqifa, would you have accepted the result of their consultation, or would you have insisted that only a direct command from the Prophet could decide the matter? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on textual certainty versus trust in collective reasoning?

Opinions on Prophetic Designation of a Successor
Lists opinions on nass and defines nass khafi and nass jali

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different positions on whether the Prophet (SAW) explicitly designated a successor, and the distinction between hidden and clear designation (nass khafi and nass jali).

Core Idea
Was the Prophet's successor explicitly named? Most say no; Shi'a say yes with clear texts.

This passage surveys the major Islamic schools on the question of prophetic designation of an imam. It presents the majority view that there was no explicit text, then discusses minority views that Abu Bakr or Ali were designated. Crucially, it defines two types of designation—hidden and clear—and gives examples from hadith. This sets the foundation for understanding the Sunni position on imama.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main positions
Read the passage and note the three positions: no designation, designation of Abu Bakr (hidden or clear), and designation of Ali.
The majority (Ash'aris, Mu'tazila, Khawarij) hold there was no designation.
2
Understand hidden vs clear designation
Focus on the definitions of nass khafi and nass jali. Hidden is not necessarily known in its intent; clear is unambiguous.
Al-Hasan al-Basri considered Abu Bakr's leading prayer a hidden designation.
3
Review examples for clear designation of Ali
Examine the four hadith cited as clear designation for Ali. Notice the phrases: 'Greet him with Commander of the Faithful', 'This is my successor after me', etc.
These are accepted by Imamiyya but not Zaydiyya.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why this debate matters: it underpins Sunni/Shi'a divergence on leadership. The passage shows that for Sunnis, no explicit text exists, so leadership is by consensus and election.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب جمهور أصحابنا والمعتزلة، والخوارج إلى ان النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) لم ينص على إمام بعده . وقيل : نص على أبي بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه فقال الحسن البصري: نصاً خفياً، وهو تقديمه إياه في الصلاة . وقال بعض أصحاب الحديث : نصاً جلياً، وهو ما روي أنه (عليه السلام) قال : ائتوني بدواة وقرطاس أكتب لأبي بكر كتاباً لا يختلف فيه اثنان ، ثم قال : يأبى الله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر . وقيل : نص على علي (رضي الله تعالى عنه . وهو مذهب الشيعة . أما النص الخفي، وهو الذي لا يعلم المراد منه بالضرورة فبالاتفاق، وأما النص الجلي فعند الإمامية دون الزيدية، وهو قوله : سلموا عليه بإمرة المؤمنين . وقوله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) مشيراً إليه وأخذاً بيده هذا خليفتي فيكم من بعدي، فاسمعوا له وأطيعوا وقوله (صلى الله عليه وسلم): أنت الخليفة من بعدي . وقوله () وقد جمع بني عبد المطلب : أيكم يبايعني ويؤازرني يكن أخي ووصيي وخليفتي من بعدي. فبايعه علي (رضي الله عنه)
The majority of our companions (Ash'aris), the Mu'tazila, and the Khawarij hold that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not designate (naṣṣa) an imam after him. It is also said: He designated Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him). Al-Hasan al-Basri said: a hidden designation (naṣṣan khafiyyan), which is his appointing him to lead the prayer. Some hadith scholars said: a clear designation (naṣṣan jaliyyan), which is the report that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Bring me an inkpot and a sheet so that I may write for Abu Bakr a document after which two will not disagree' then he said: 'Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' And it is said: He designated 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) – that is the doctrine of the Shi'a. As for the hidden designation, which is not necessarily known in its intent, there is agreement (on its being accepted). As for the clear designation, it is held by the Imamiyya but not the Zaydiyya, and it is his statement: 'Greet him with the title of Commander of the Faithful' and his statement (peace be upon him) pointing to him and taking his hand: 'This is my successor (khalīfatī) among you after me, so listen to him and obey' and his statement (peace be upon him): 'You are the caliph after me' and his statement – having gathered the Banu 'Abd al-Muttalib –: 'Which of you will pledge allegiance to me and support me will be my brother, my executor (waṣiyyī) and my successor after me.' So 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) pledged allegiance to him.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents the various positions on whether the Prophet (SAW) explicitly designated (naṣṣa) a successor (imam) after him. It begins by stating that the majority of Ash'aris, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij hold that there was no such designation. Then it mentions two minority views: one that the Prophet designated Abu Bakr in a hidden manner (naṣṣ khafī) – i.e., his leading the prayer – and another that he made a clear designation (naṣṣ jalī) of Abu Bakr based on the incident of the inkpot and the statement 'Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' Then it notes the Shi'a view that the Prophet explicitly designated 'Ali. The passage then defines the two types of designation: hidden (khafī) which is agreed upon, and clear (jalī) which the Imamiyya affirm but the Zaydiyya do not. It provides examples of clear designation from hadith: greeting 'Ali as Commander of the Faithful, the statement 'this is my successor after me', 'you are the caliph after me', and the gathering of Banu 'Abd al-Muttalib where 'Ali pledged allegiance. This sets the stage for the subsequent Sunni proof.

Key Terms
نص
نص خفي
نص جلي
إمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hidden designation (nass khafi) provides a valid scriptural basis for appointing a successor.
Correction: The passage clarifies that hidden designation is not necessarily known in its intent, and the majority does not consider it a clear textual command. It is merely an inference, not a definitive proof.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Ash'aris, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij, what is the status of the Prophet's designation of a successor?
A) He designated Abu Bakr clearly
B) He designated 'Ali clearly
C) He did not designate anyone
D) He designated both Abu Bakr and 'Ali

Key Takeaway
The majority of Sunni schools hold that the Prophet did not leave an explicit textual designation of his successor, while the Shi'a claim clear texts for Ali, which this passage enumerates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage presents conflicting claims about whether the Prophet explicitly named a successor. When you consider that early Muslims disagreed on this foundational issue, does it unsettle your sense of certainty about Islamic history? Can you accept that ambiguity, or do you feel compelled to choose one side?
?
If you were among the companions at the Prophet's death, would you have insisted on a clear text (nass jali) before accepting a leader, or would you have trusted the community's consensus? What does your answer reveal about your own reliance on textual authority versus communal reasoning?
?
The Shi'a cite four specific statements from the Prophet as clear designations of Ali. If you believe these reports are authentic, what practical obligations follow for you today? If you doubt their authenticity, how do you reconcile that doubt with the fact that many sincere Muslims built their entire faith on these texts? Do you see that as a challenge to your own criteria for accepting hadith?
