The Claim of Concealment and Its Refutation
Author presents an objection and answer about concealment of the nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objection raised against the Companions regarding the concealment of the nass and the author's refutation based on their character and Ali's conduct.

Core Idea
The Companions' piety and Ali's later actions refute the claim that they concealed the explicit text.

In this passage, the author engages with a common Shia objection that the Companions knew about the explicit designation of Ali as caliph but concealed it for worldly motives. The objection lists several alleged reasons, including love of leadership, envy, and even the possibility of abrogation. The author responds by appealing to the known righteousness of the Companions and the inconsistency of Ali's supposed silence with his later assertiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Begin by reading the opening objection that lists the motives for concealment. Note the specific accusations: love of leadership, hatred, envy, and the claim of abrogation.
The objection also states that Ali himself practiced taqiyya.
2
Analyze the refutation's first part
The author answers by asserting that anyone with piety knows the Companions are innocent. He argues from their divine selection and renunciation of worldly pleasures.
The argument uses a 'how could it be' rhetorical style.
3
Examine the focus on Ali's conduct
The refutation then zeroes in on Ali, arguing that his later boldness in claiming his rights contradicts the idea that he would abandon his right out of taqiyya earlier, especially when conditions were more favorable.
The footnote defines 'naskh' for clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : علموا ذلك وكتموه لأغراض لهم في ذلك ، كحب الرياسة ، والحقد على علي رضي الله تعالى عنه لقتله أقرباءهم وعشائرهم، وحسدهم إياه على ما له من المناقب، والكمالات وشدة الاختصاص بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وظنهم أن النص قد لحقه النسخ (١) لما رأوا من ترك كبار الصحابة العمل به، إلى غير ذلك، وترك علي (رضي الله عنه المحاجة به تقية وخوفاً من الأعداء وقلة وثوق بقبول الجماعة. قلنا : من كان له حظ من الديانة والإنصاف علم قطعاً براءة أصحاب رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وجلالة أقدارهم عن مخالفة امره في مثل هذا الخطب الجليل، ومتابعة الهوى، وترك الدليل، واتباع خطوات الشيطان والضلال عن سواء السبيل، وكيف بظن بجماعة رضي الله عنهم ، وآثرهم الله لصحبة رسوله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) ونصرة دينه ، ووصفهم بكونهم خير أمة أخرجت للناس ، يأمرون بالمعروف، وينهون عن المنكر، وقد تواتر منهم الإعراض عن متاع الدنيا وطيباتها وزخارفها ومستلذاتها، والإقبال على بذل جهم وذخائرهم ، وقتل أقاربهم وعشائرهم في نصرة رسول الله ، وإقامة شريعته، و انقياد أمره واتباع طريقته ، أنهم خالفوه قبل أن يدفنوه وتركوا هداهم ، واتبعوا هواهم، وعدلوا عن الحق الصحيح إلى الباطل الصريح وخذلوا مستحقاً من بني هاشم و خاص ذوي القربى إلى غاصب من بني تيم أو عدي بن كعب، وأن مثل علي (رضي الله عنه مع صلابته في الدين .وبسالته . وشدة شكيمته وقوة عزيمته، وغلو شأنه، وكثرة ،أعوانه وكون أكثر المهاجرين والأنصار والرؤساء الكبار معه قد ترك حقه، وسلم الأمر لمن لا يستحقه من شيخ من بني تيم ضعيف الحال، عديم المال، قليل الأتباع والأشياع ، ولم يقم بأمره ، وطلب حقه، كما قام به حين أفضي إليه وقاتل من نازعه بكلتا يديه حتى فني الخلق الكثير والجم الغفير، وآثر على التقية عن الحمية في الدين، والعصبية للإسلام والمسلمين ، مع أن الخطب إذ ذاك أشد، والخصم ألد . وفي أول الأمر قلوب القوم أرق، وجانبهم أسهل، واراؤهم إلى اتباع الحق واجتذاب الباطل أميل ، وعهدهم بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أقوى، وهمهم في تنفيذ أحكامه أرغب . (١) النسخ في اللغة: عبارة عن التبديل والرفع والإزالة يقال : نسخت الشمس الظل أزالته ، وفي الشريعة، هو بيان انتهاء الحكم الشرعي في حق صاحب الشرع ، وكان انتهاؤه عند الله تعالى معلوماً إلا أن في علمنا كان استمراره ودوامه وبالناسخ علمنا انتهاؤه وكان في حقنا تبديلاً وتغييراً.
If it is said: They knew it and concealed it for their own purposes, such as love of leadership, hatred of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) for killing their relatives and clans, envying him for his merits, perfections, and strong connection to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and their assumption that the text had been abrogated (1) because they saw senior companions abandoning it, among other things, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) refrained from arguing with it out of dissimulation (taqiyya) and fear of enemies and lack of confidence in acceptance by the community. We say: Whoever has a share of piety and fairness knows with certainty the innocence of the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and the majesty of their ranks from opposing his command in such a great matter, following desire, abandoning evidence, following the steps of Satan, and straying from the straight path. How could it be supposed of a group, may Allah be pleased with them, whom Allah chose for the companionship of His Messenger (peace be upon him) and the support of His religion, and described them as the best community brought forth for mankind, enjoining good and forbidding evil, and from whom there is continuous transmission (tawātur) of turning away from the pleasures of the world and its adornments and delights, and of expending their wealth and treasures, killing their relatives and clans in support of the Messenger of Allah, establishing his law, submitting to his command and following his way, that they opposed him before burying him, abandoned their guidance, followed their desires, turned from true truth to clear falsehood, and betrayed a rightful claimant from Banū Hāshim and the close relatives to an usurper from Banū Taym or ʿAdī ibn Kaʿb? And that someone like Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), with his firmness in religion, his valor, his strong resolve, his powerful determination, his high station, his many supporters, and the fact that most of the Muhājirūn, Anṣār, and great leaders were with him, abandoned his right and surrendered the matter to one who did not deserve it, a weak old man from Banū Taym without wealth, with few followers and partisans, and did not stand up for his matter or demand his right, as he did when it became his turn and he fought those who disputed him with both hands until many people and a great multitude perished, and he preferred dissimulation (taqiyya) over zeal for religion, partisanship for Islam and Muslims, even though the situation at that time was more severe, the opponent more obstinate, and at the beginning the hearts of the people were softer, their side easier, their opinions more inclined to follow truth and repel falsehood, their covenant with the Prophet (peace be upon him) stronger, and their desire to implement his rulings greater. (1) Al-naskh in language is change, removal, and elimination; it is said: the sun abrogated the shadow, i.e., removed it. In sharīʿa, it is the clarification of the end of a legal ruling in the right of the Lawgiver, while its end was known to Allah, except that in our knowledge there was its continuation and permanence, and by the abrogating verse we know its end, and it was in our right a change and alteration.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer refutation of the claim that the Companions knew about the explicit textual designation (nass jali) of Ali but concealed it for worldly reasons. The objection lists several alleged motives: love of leadership, hatred of Ali for killing their relatives, envy of his merits, belief that the text was abrogated, etc. It also claims that Ali himself refrained from arguing with it out of taqiyya and fear. The answer begins by affirming that anyone with piety and fairness knows the Companions were innocent of such moral failure. The author then argues from their known character: they were chosen by Allah for companionship, described as the best community, and known for renouncing worldly pleasures and sacrificing their wealth and lives. It would be impossible for such people to oppose the Prophet's command before his burial and follow desire. The answer then focuses on Ali: given his firmness, bravery, numerous supporters, and later fighting for his rights when caliphate came to him, it is inconceivable that he would have abandoned his right out of taqiyya if he truly had an explicit text. The author concludes that the situation was more favorable earlier, making taqiyya implausible. The footnote defines al-naskh linguistically and technically.

Key Terms
النص الجلي
التقية
الصحابة
النسخ
الإعراض عن الدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqiyya was a valid excuse for Ali's silence.
Correction: The author argues that Ali's later boldness in claiming his rights contradicts the idea that he would practice taqiyya earlier, especially when conditions were more favorable.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the answer in this passage?
A) The Companions were righteous and could not have concealed the truth.
B) Ali was weak and afraid to claim his right.
C) The text was indeed abrogated.
D) The Shia are correct but the majority rejected it.

Key Takeaway
The claim that the Companions concealed the nass is refuted by their eminent character and Ali's own conduct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself quick to assume bad motives of the Companions or other Muslims when their actions don't align with your understanding? How does this lesson's defense of their character challenge your own tendency to judge?
?
Ali (ra) is said to have refrained from asserting his right out of taqiyya, yet the author argues this is inconsistent with his later boldness. When have you used fear or circumstance as an excuse to avoid standing for truth? Will you commit to examining your own hesitations in light of Ali's example?
?
The Companions are described as turning away from worldly pleasures. In what area of your life are you still holding onto a worldly desire that may be clouding your judgment about truth? How will you actively cultivate detachment?

Implications of Claiming an Explicit Text
The author enumerates the slanders implied by claiming nass jali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming an explicit text (nass jali) for Ali's succession leads to slander against key Islamic figures and texts.

Core Idea
Claiming nass jali leads to slander against the Companions, Ali, the Prophet, and the Quran.

This passage presents a powerful argument against the claim that there was an explicit text (nass jali) designating Ali as the Prophet's successor. The author shows that such a claim necessarily implies slandering multiple parties, including the senior Companions, Ali himself, the Prophet, and even the Quran. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the Sunni position on the caliphate and the integrity of the early Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the parallel structure: 'slandered X, and Y, ...'
2
Identify the four parties slandered
The passage lists four groups or individuals who would be slandered by the claim of nass jali. Find each one and note the specific accusation leveled against them.
The parties are: the Muhajirun and Ansar, Ali, the Prophet, and the Quran.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself why each of these slanders follows necessarily from the claim. For example, why does claiming nass jali imply that Ali followed falsehood?
The logic is that if the Prophet explicitly designated Ali, then those who opposed him (the Muhajirun and Ansar) concealed the truth, and Ali himself failed to act on it.
4
Connect to broader theology
Consider how this argument protects the integrity of the Quran and the Prophet's judgment. The Quran praises the Companions, so the claim of nass jali contradicts explicit Quranic praise.
This shows that the claim is not just a historical error but a theological deviation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ادعى النص الجلي فقد طعن في كبار المهاجرين، والأنصار عامة، بمخالفة الحق وكتمانه وفي علي رضي الله تعالى عنه خاصة باتباعه الباطل وإذعانه بل في النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) حيث اتخذ القوم أحباباً . وأصحاباً، وأعوانــاً وأنصاراً، وأختاناً ، وأصهاراً، مع علمه بحالهم في ابتدائهم ومالهم ، بل في كتاب الله تعالى، حيث أثنى عليهم، وجعلهم خير أمة، ووصفهم بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي المنكر.
And whoever claims the explicit text (al-nass al-jali) has indeed slandered the senior Muhājirūn and the Anṣār in general, by (accusing them of) opposing the truth and concealing it, and especially slandered Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) by (accusing him of) following falsehood and submitting to it, and indeed slandered the Prophet (peace be upon him) for taking these people as beloved ones, companions, helpers, in-laws, and relatives, while knowing their condition from their beginning and what they were, and indeed slandered the Book of Allah, where He praised them, made them the best community, and described them as enjoining good and forbidding evil.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument showing the implications of claiming an explicit text (nass jali) designating Ali. The author states that such a claim necessarily involves slandering several parties. First, it slanders the senior Muhajirun and Ansar generally, accusing them of opposing the truth and concealing it. Second, it slanders Ali specifically, accusing him of following falsehood and submitting to it (since he did not act on the supposed text). Third, it slanders the Prophet, who took these people as companions, helpers, and relatives despite knowing their character. Fourth, it slanders the Quran, which praises the Companions as the best community and describes them as enjoining good and forbidding evil. Thus, the claim of nass jali is not just a historical error but leads to blasphemy against the Quran and the Prophet.

Key Terms
النص الجلي
الطعن
المهاجرون
الأنصار
خير أمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Claiming nass jali is a minor historical claim about succession.
Correction: The passage shows it implies slander against the Companions, Ali, the Prophet, and the Quran, making it a major theological deviation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, claiming an explicit text (nass jali) leads to slandering all of the following EXCEPT:
A) The senior Muhajirun and Ansar
B) Ali ibn Abi Talib
C) The Prophet Muhammad
D) The first three caliphs

Key Takeaway
Claiming an explicit text for Ali's succession logically entails slander against the Companions, Ali, the Prophet, and the Quran, thus refuting the claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a theological opinion that, if fully thought through, would lead to criticism of the Prophet or the Quran? What would it cost you to abandon that opinion today?
?
The author shows that a false claim leads to slandering entire groups of people. Are there claims you make about others—whether about individuals or communities—that, when traced to their logical end, slander even the Prophet's companions? Will you investigate and uproot such claims this week?

The Explicit Text Claim Is a Fabrication
Refutes the Shia claim of explicit designation, attributing it to later fabricators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim of an explicit textual designation of Ali as successor (an-naṣṣ al-jalī) is considered a fabrication by Sunni scholars, based on historical and textual evidence.

Core Idea
The explicit text claim was invented by later heretics, not transmitted by the Prophet.

The Shia doctrine of an explicit designation of Ali as the Prophet's successor is a central point of contention. In this passage, the author argues that this claim lacks historical credibility, as it was unknown among early Muslims and was fabricated by later individuals. Let's examine the evidence presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the author's tone and the key points he raises.
The passage uses strong language like 'among the obstinacies'.
2
Identify the historical arguments
The author argues that the explicit text was not known among the Companions and Successors, and no reliable hadith scholar transmitted it. Find these points in the text.
3
Consider the testimony of Ibn Jarir al-Tabari
Even a scholar accused of Shi'ism did not include the addition. What does this suggest about the claim?
This is a significant argument from silence.
4
Understand the origin of the doctrine
The author attributes the invention to Hisham ibn al-Hakam and his followers. Why might this be significant?
Consider the implications for the reliability of the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مكابرات الروافض ادعاؤهم تواتر هذا النص قرناً بعد قرناً، مع أنه لم يشتهر فيما بين الصحابة والتابعين . ولم يثبت ممن يوثق به من المحدثين، مع شدة ميلهم إلى أمير المؤمنين ونقلهم الأحاديث الكثيرة في مناقبه وكمالاته في أمر الدنيا والدين، ولم ينقل عنه (رضي الله تعالى عنه) في خطبه ورسائله ومفاخره إشارة إلى ذلك . وابن جرير الطبري مع اتهامه بالتشيع لم يذكر في روايته قصة الدار هذه الزيادة التي يدعيها الشيعة وهي قوله (صلى الله عليه وسلم): «إنه خليفتي فيكم من بعدي...» ونعم ما قال المأمون: وجدت أربعة في أربعة: الزهد في المعتزلة، والكذب في الرافضة، والمروءة في أصحاب الحديث، وحب الرياسة في أصحاب الرأي. والظاهر ما ذكره المتكلمون من أن هذا المذهب أعني دعوى النص الجلي مما وضعه هشام بن الحكم، ونصره ابن الراوندي وأبو عيسى الوراق وأضرابهم، ثم رواه أسلاف الروافض شغفاً بتقرير مذهبهم.
And among the obstinacies of the Rafidah is their claim of the tawatur (widespread transmission) of this text (an-naṣṣ) century after century, despite that it was not well-known among the Companions and the Successors. And it was not established by reliable hadith scholars, despite their intense inclination towards the Commander of the Faithful and their transmission of many hadiths about his merits and perfections in worldly and religious matters, and nothing was transmitted from him (may Allah be pleased with him) in his sermons, letters, and boasts alluding to that. And Ibn Jarir al-Tabari, despite being accused of Shi'ism, did not mention in his narration of the story of the house (qissa al-dār) this addition that the Shi'a claim, namely his saying (peace be upon him): 'He is my successor (khalīfatī) among you after me...' And excellent is what al-Ma'mun said: I found four things in four: asceticism in the Mu'tazila, lying in the Rafidah, manliness in the People of Hadith, and love of leadership in the People of Opinion. And what is apparent is what the theologians (al-mutakallimūn) mentioned: that this doctrine, i.e., the claim of the explicit text (an-naṣṣ al-jalī), was invented by Hisham ibn al-Hakam, and supported by Ibn al-Rawandi and Abu 'Isa al-Warraq and their ilk, then the predecessors of the Rafidah narrated it out of eagerness to establish their doctrine.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a direct refutation of the Shia claim that there was an explicit textual designation of 'Ali as successor. The author argues that the supposed widespread transmission (tawatur) of this text is a lie, because it was not known among the Companions and Successors, and no reliable narrator transmitted it. Even Ibn Jarir al-Tabari, despite his Shia leanings, did not include this addition in his account. The author then quotes al-Ma'mun's aphorism that lying is found among the Rafidah. Finally, he states that the theologians have identified the origin of this doctrine: it was invented by Hisham ibn al-Hakam and propagated by later heretics, not by the Prophet.

Key Terms
النص الجلي (an-naṣṣ al-jalī)
التواتر (at-tawātur)
الروافض (ar-rawāfiḍ)
هشام بن الحكم
ابن جرير الطبري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The explicit text claim was widely accepted by early Muslims.
Correction: The passage shows it was unknown among Companions and Successors and was later fabricated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who invented the doctrine of the explicit text (النص الجلي)?
A) Ibn Jarir al-Tabari
B) Hisham ibn al-Hakam
C) Al-Ma'mun
D) The Companions

Key Takeaway
The claim of explicit designation (النص الجلي) is historically unfounded and was fabricated by later heretic figures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim that contradicts solid historical evidence, do you pause to verify it, or do you accept it because it supports your preferences? In what area of your life do you most need to confront this tendency today?
?
The passage accuses the Rafidah of lying to support their doctrine. Is there an area in your own life where you have exaggerated or invented a narrative to defend your own position or group? Will you repent and align with the truth, even if uncomfortable?
?
If the Prophet's explicit successor was unknown to the Companions and even to Ali himself, what does that tell you about your own need to follow the early community's understanding? Are you willing to trust the consensus of the Salaf over later innovations?

Imam al-Razi's Argument Against Tawatur
Al-Razi enumerates three reasons why the Shia claim of tawatur is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's three-pronged argument showing the Shia claim of tawatur for the explicit text is self-contradictory.

Core Idea
Al-Razi shows the claim is self-contradictory because if most Muslims apostatized, too few transmitters remain for tawatur.

Imam al-Razi presents a powerful critique of the Shia claim that the explicit text on succession was transmitted through tawatur. He finds it astonishing on three counts, each undermining the possibility of widespread transmission. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and reveals the logical flaw at the heart of the claim.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Razi's statement
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its English translation. Notice the tone of astonishment and the three groups al-Razi distinguishes.
The passage is a single sentence with three 'an' clauses.
2
Identify the three groups
Al-Razi mentions three categories: the perfect scholars (al-kāmilūn), the commoners/middling (al-ʿawāmm wa awsāṭ), and the extremists (al-ghulāt). Understand what he says about each.
Each group presents a separate obstacle to tawatur.
3
Understand the logical contradiction
Focus on the extremists' claim that most Muslims apostatized. If only a handful remained, how could there be widespread transmission? This is the key self-contradiction.
Tawatur requires many independent transmitters in every generation.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider why al-Razi finds this claim 'astonishing'. The claim of tawatur is incompatible with the claim of mass apostasy. This argument shows internal inconsistency in the Shia position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الرازي: ومن العجائب أن الكاملين من علماء الشيعة لم يبلغوا كل عصر حد الكثرة فضلاً عن التواتر وأن عوامهم وأوساطهم لا يقدرون أن يفهموا كيفية هذه الدعوى على الوجه المحقق، وأن غلاتهم زعموا أن المسلمين ارتدوا بعد النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) ولم يبق على الإسلام إلا عدد يسير أقل من العشرة، فكيف يدعون التواتر في ذلك الطريق.
Imam al-Razi said: Among the wonders is that the perfect ones among the Shia scholars did not in any era reach the limit of multitude, let alone tawatur; and that their commoners and middle ones cannot understand the reality of this claim in a verified manner; and that their extremists claimed that the Muslims apostatized after the Prophet (peace be upon him) and only a small number less than ten remained upon Islam. So how can they claim tawatur in that way?
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from Imam al-Razi against the Shia claim of widespread transmission (tawatur) of the explicit text. He finds it astonishing for three reasons: first, the number of competent Shia scholars has never been large enough to constitute tawatur; second, even the average Shia cannot properly understand the claim; third, the extremists among them claim that most Muslims apostatized after the Prophet, leaving only a handful. If apostasy was so widespread, there would be too few transmitters to achieve tawatur. Thus the claim is self-contradictory.

Key Terms
التواتر (at-tawātur)
العلماء (al-ʿulamāʾ)
الغلاة (al-ghulāt)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That tawatur simply requires many narrators, regardless of generation.
Correction: Al-Razi shows tawatur requires many reliable transmitters in every generation; the extremists' claim of mass apostasy eliminates the possibility of a continuous chain.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, why is the claim of tawatur of the explicit text contradictory?
A) Because the Shia scholars are many
B) Because Shia extremists claim most Muslims apostatized, leaving few transmitters
C) Because the text is in the Quran
D) Because all Companions agreed on it

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi argues that the Shia claim of tawatur is self-defeating because their own extremists claim near-total apostasy, leaving insufficient transmitters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals how a belief's own extremists can undermine its evidence. Are there any opinions you hold that, if pushed to their logical extreme, would contradict your foundational beliefs? Are you brave enough to follow that logic wherever it leads, even if it means letting go of cherished ideas?
?
Al-Razi uses rigorous intellectual consistency to refute a claim. When was the last time you applied that same consistency to your own understanding of a religious issue? What uncomfortable conclusion might you be avoiding by not doing so?
?
If the Shia extremists believed only a handful remained Muslims, that destroyed their claim of widespread transmission. How often do you accept arguments from people without checking whether their own premises undermine their conclusion? Will you commit today to examining the internal consistency of every religious claim you hear, especially from those you trust?

Evidences from the Companions Against an Explicit Text
Lists three Companions' statements that imply no explicit text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the actions and statements of key Companions (al-Abbas, Umar, and Abu Bakr) indicate that there was no explicit text designating Ali as successor.

Core Idea
The silence and alternative suggestions of the Companions prove no explicit text existed.

This lesson examines the first set of historical evidences from the source: the statements of al-Abbas, Umar, and Abu Bakr. These Companions either offered allegiance to others or expressed uncertainty about the succession, which would be impossible if a clear text existed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice how each evidence is introduced with 'قول' (saying).
2
Identify each evidence
List the three evidences: al-Abbas offering allegiance to Ali, Umar offering allegiance to Abu Ubayda, and Abu Bakr suggesting Umar or Abu Ubayda, plus his regret.
3
Understand the implication
Why does each evidence imply absence of text? If there was a text, these actions would be rebellion or ignorance.
The author argues that together they yield certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - روايات وأمارات ربما تفيد باجتماعها القطع بعدم النص، وهي كثيرة جداً كقول العباس لعلي : امدد يدك أبايعك . تقول الناس : هذا رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) بايع ابن عمه فلا يختلف عليك اثنان. وقول عمر لأبي عبيدة (رضي الله تعالى عنه) : امدد يدك أبايعك. وقول أبي بكر : بايعوا عمر أو أبا عبيدة. وقوله : وددت أني سألت النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) عن هذا الأمر فيمن هو، وكنا لا ننازعه. وكدخول علي رضي الله تعالى عنه في الشورى، فإنه رضي بإمامة أيهم كان. وكقوله (رضي الله تعالى عنه) لطلحة (رضي الله تعالى عنه): إن أردت بايعتك. وكاحتجاجه على معاوية ببيعة الناس له، لا بنص من النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم). وكقوله حين دعي إلى البيعة: اتركوني والتمسوا غيري. وكمعاضدته أبا بكر وعمر والإشارة عليهما بما هو أصلح حين خرج أبو بكر لقتال العرب وعمر لقتال فارس. وكعدم تعرضه لذلك النص في شيء من خطبه ورسائله ومفاخراته ومخاصماته، وعند تأخره عن البيعة. وكإنكار زيد بن علي مع علو رتبته هذا النص، وكذا كثير من سادات أهل البيت. وكتسمية الصحابة أبا بكر مدة حياته بخليفة رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم).
The second [way] — narrations and indications that together perhaps yield certainty of the absence of the text. They are very many, such as: the saying of al-Abbas to Ali: 'Extend your hand so that I may pledge allegiance to you, and people will say: This is the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) pledging allegiance to his cousin, so no two will differ over you.' And the saying of Umar to Abu Ubayda (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Extend your hand so that I may pledge allegiance to you.' And the saying of Abu Bakr: 'Pledge allegiance to Umar or Abu Ubayda.' And his saying: 'I wish I had asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about this matter — whom it is for — and we would not dispute it.' And Ali's (may Allah be pleased with him) entry into the shura (council), for he was pleased with the leadership of whichever of them was chosen. And his saying (may Allah be pleased with him) to Talha (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If you wish, I will pledge allegiance to you.' And his argument against Muawiya based on the people's pledge of allegiance to him, not on a text from the Prophet (peace be upon him). And his saying when he was called to the pledge of allegiance: 'Leave me and seek someone else.' And his support for Abu Bakr and Umar and his advice to them regarding what was more beneficial when Abu Bakr went out to fight the Arabs and Umar to fight Persia. And his failure to mention that text in any of his sermons, letters, boasts, or disputes, and when he delayed from the pledge. And the denial of Zayd ibn Ali, despite his high rank, of this text, as well as many of the leaders of the Ahl al-Bayt. And the Companions' calling Abu Bakr during his lifetime the Successor (khalifa) of the Messenger of God.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage provides the second argument: a collection of historical evidences that collectively prove there was no explicit text designating Ali. The author enumerates many examples: al-Abbas offered to pledge allegiance to Ali, implying the matter was open; Umar and Abu Bakr suggested other candidates; Abu Bakr regretted not asking the Prophet; Ali participated in the shura (consultation council), accepted any outcome, offered to pledge allegiance to Talha, argued with Muawiya based on public pledge (not text), and initially refused the caliphate. Ali also supported Abu Bakr and Umar, never mentioned any explicit text, and Zayd ibn Ali and other Ahl al-Bayt figures denied it. Finally, the Companions called Abu Bakr 'Khalifat Rasul Allah' during his lifetime, indicating no one believed in a prior exclusive designation.

Key Terms
النص (an-naṣṣ)
البيعة (al-bayʿa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Abu Bakr say he wished he had done?
A) Asked the Prophet about the succession
B) Appointed Ali directly
C) Consulted more people
D) Written a will

Key Takeaway
The actions of key Companions, such as suggesting alternative candidates and expressing uncertainty, collectively indicate that no explicit text designating Ali was known.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in Abu Bakr's position, knowing that the Prophet hadn't clearly named a successor, would you have been content to suggest other candidates, or would you have insisted on waiting for divine guidance? What does your answer reveal about your trust in human judgment versus revealed text?
?
The Companions acted on their best understanding, yet later generations fought over this very issue. Are you willing to admit that you might be wrong about a matter you hold dear, just as Abu Bakr wished he had asked the Prophet? What belief are you most afraid to question?
?
Al-Abbas expected that people would follow Ali because of his relation to the Prophet. Have you ever relied on your lineage, status, or reputation to gain acceptance rather than on truth? Repent and resolve to seek truth regardless of who advocates it.

Ali's Conduct and Other Indications Against an Explicit Text
Lists Ali's own conduct and other indications that there was no explicit text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali's own actions and statements, as well as the conduct of later figures, further demonstrate the absence of an explicit text.

Core Idea
Ali's participation in shura, offering allegiance to others, and never mentioning the text prove no explicit text existed.

This lesson covers the remaining evidences from the source: Ali's entry into the shura council, his offer to pledge allegiance to Talha, his argument with Muawiya based on public allegiance, his initial refusal of the caliphate, his support for Abu Bakr and Umar, and his silence about any text. Additionally, Zayd ibn Ali and other Ahl al-Bayt figures denied the text, and the Companions called Abu Bakr 'Khalifa' during his lifetime.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the second part of the source, focusing on Ali's actions and the final two evidences.
2
Group the evidences
Categorize: (a) Ali's actions in shura, offering to Talha, arguing with Muawiya, refusing, supporting; (b) Ali's failure to mention the text; (c) Zayd's denial; (d) Companions calling Abu Bakr khalifa.
3
Analyze each evidence
Consider how each point directly contradicts the claim that there was an explicit text designating Ali.

?

The Implausibility of Tawatur for the Shi'a Claim
Al-Razi critiques the possibility of tawatur for the Shi'a claim of an explicit text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi argues that the Shi'a claim of an explicit text for Ali's succession cannot be supported by tawatur, given the lack of widespread transmission and the internal contradictions of the Shi'a position.

Core Idea
A claim of mass transmission cannot rest on a tiny scholarly elite.

Al-Razi begins his refutation by pointing out the improbability of the Shi'a claim of tawatur (mass transmission) regarding an explicit text designating Ali. He notes that only a few expert Shi'a scholars exist in each age, far from the number required for tawatur, and that their extremists believe most companions apostatized, which would actually undermine any claim of continuous transmission. This lesson examines these logical and historical inconsistencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Read the opening sentence to see what al-Razi is addressing: the Shi'a claim of a nass (explicit text) for Ali's succession.
Notice that he begins with 'From among the wonders' to highlight the absurdity.
2
Understand the first problem: lack of tawatur
Al-Razi says the perfect scholars among the Shi'a have never reached the level of multitude in any age, let alone tawatur. This is a numerical argument.
Tawatur requires a large number of reliable transmitters in every generation.
3
Consider the second problem: ignorance of common Shi'a
The common and middle-level Shi'a cannot even understand the claim properly, which means it cannot be widely known.
4
Analyze the third problem: extremist views
The extremists claim that most companions apostatized, leaving fewer than ten Muslims. If that were true, there could be no continuous transmission from the Prophet's time.
This is self-defeating for the claim of tawatur.
5
Conclude the argument
Al-Razi sums up by asking how they can claim tawatur given these problems.
The rhetorical question reinforces the impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الرازي: ومن العجائب أن الكاملين من علماء الشيعة لم يبلغوا كل عصر حد الكثرة فضلاً عن التواتر وأن عوامهم وأوساطهم لا يقدرون أن يفهموا كيفية هذه الدعوى على الوجه المحقق، وأن غلاتهم زعموا أن المسلمين ارتدوا بعد النبي ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) ولم يبق على الإسلام إلا عدد يسير أقل من العشرة ، فكيف يدعون التواتر في ذلك الطريق . الثاني - روايات وأمارات ربما تفيد باجتماعها القطع بعدم النص، وهي كثيرة جداً كقول العباس لعلي : امدد يدك أبايعك . تقول الناس : هذا رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) بايع ابن عمه فلا يختلف عليك اثنان. وقول عمر لأبي عبيدة (رضي الله تعالى عنه) : امدد يدك أبايعك. وقول أبي بكر : بايعوا عمر أو أبا عبيدة. وقوله : وددت أني سألت النبي ( ) عن هذا الأمر فيمن هو ، وكنا لا ننازعه وكدخول علي رضي الله تعالى عنه في الشورى، فإنه رضي بإمامة أيهم كان. وكقوله (رضي الله تعالى عنه) لطلحة (رضي الله تعالى عنه : إن أردت بايعتك وكاحتجاجه على معاوية ببيعة الناس له، لا بنص من النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وكقوله حين دعي إلى البيعة : اتركوني والتمسوا غيري، وكمعاضدته أبا بكر وعمر والإشارة عليهما بما هو أصلح حين خرج أبو بكر لقتال العرب وعمر لقتال فارس وكعدم تعرضه لذلك النص في شيء من خطبه ورسائله ومفاخراته ومخاصماته، وعند تأخره عن البيعة، وكإنكار زيد بن علي مع علو رتبته هذا النص، وكذا كثير من سادات أهل البيت. وكتسمية الصحابة أبا بكر مدة حياته بخليفة رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم ) .
Al-Imam al-Razi said: Among the wonders is that the perfect ones among the Shi'a scholars have not reached in every age the limit of multitude, let alone tawatur (mass transmission), and their common people and middle ones are not able to understand how this claim is in a verified manner, and their extremists claimed that the Muslims apostatized after the Prophet (peace be upon him) and there remained upon Islam only a number less than ten, so how do they claim tawatur in that path? Second: Narrations and indications that perhaps together yield certainty of the absence of nass (explicit text), and they are very many, like the statement of al-Abbas to Ali: Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you. The people would say: This is the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) pledging allegiance to his cousin, so two would not differ over you. And the statement of Umar to Abu Ubayda (may God be pleased with him): Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you. And the statement of Abu Bakr: Pledge allegiance to Umar or Abu Ubayda. And his statement: I wish that I had asked the Prophet ( ) about this matter as to whom it belongs, and we would not dispute him. And Ali's (may God be pleased with him) entry into the shura (consultation council), for he was pleased with the imamate of whichever of them it was. And his statement (may God be pleased with him) to Talha (may God be pleased with him): If you wish, I will pledge allegiance to you. And his argument against Muawiya by the people's pledge to him, not by a text from the Prophet (peace be upon him). And his statement when summoned to the pledge: Leave me and seek someone else. And his support of Abu Bakr and Umar and his advice to them in what was more beneficial when Abu Bakr went out to fight the Arabs and Umar to fight Persia. And his not mentioning that text in any of his sermons, letters, boasts, or disputes, and at his delay of the pledge. And Zayd ibn Ali's denial, despite his high rank, of this text, and likewise many of the nobles of the Ahl al-Bayt. And the companions' naming of Abu Bakr throughout his life as the Caliph of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a claim of an explicit text (nass) designating Ali as the Prophet's successor. It begins by quoting al-Razi, who points out the improbability of tawatur for such a claim, given the small number of knowledgeable Shi'a and the extremist view that most companions apostatized, which would undermine tawatur. Then it presents the second type of evidence: numerous historical narrations and indications that together yield certainty of the absence of nass. These include al-Abbas offering to pledge allegiance to Ali to prevent disagreement, Umar's offer to Abu Ubayda, Abu Bakr's suggestion of Umar or Abu Ubayda, Ali's own statements and actions such as entering the shura council, offering allegiance to Talha, arguing with Muawiya based on general bay'a rather than nass, and even apologizing for delaying his own pledge. Additionally, Zayd ibn Ali and many other Ahl al-Bayt figures denied the existence of such a text, and the companions consistently called Abu Bakr the 'Caliph of the Messenger of God', all of which contradict the notion of an explicit designation.

Key Terms
تواتر
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Shi'a claim of an explicit text for Ali is supported by tawatur.
Correction: Al-Razi demonstrates that even according to Shi'a internal logic, the claim cannot meet the conditions of tawatur due to insufficient scholars, lack of common knowledge, and the extremist view that most companions apostatized.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, what is one reason why the Shi'a claim of tawatur for the text designating Ali is implausible?
A) The Shi'a scholars are too numerous.
B) The common Shi'a cannot understand the claim.
C) The extremists claim there were many Muslims after the Prophet.
D) The Prophet explicitly denied such a text.

Key Takeaway
The Shi'a claim of an explicit text for Ali cannot be supported by tawatur due to insufficient scholarly numbers, public ignorance, and internal self-defeating extremist beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim that is only held by a small group, how do you verify its transmission? Al-Razi shows that a small group's claim of mass transmission is self-contradictory. Is there a belief you hold that you have accepted without checking its actual transmission or support?
?
Al-Razi points out that common people could not even understand the claim properly. Do you repeat religious claims that you don't fully understand? What is one claim you will commit to studying more deeply before accepting or transmitting it?
?
The extremist belief that almost all companions apostatized would break any chain of knowledge. Have you ever entertained a belief that, if true, would undermine the very sources of your faith? Are you willing to scrutinize your own beliefs for internal consistency, even if it is uncomfortable?

Historical Evidences Against the Claim of an Explicit Text
Al-Razi enumerates historical evidences that together yield certainty of the absence of an explicit text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical evidences that al-Razi presents to demonstrate the absence of an explicit text for Ali's succession, including statements and actions of key companions.

Core Idea
Numerous historical indications collectively refute the existence of an explicit designation.

After dismantling the possibility of tawatur, al-Razi presents a second line of argument: multiple historical reports and indications that together produce certainty that no explicit text (nass) existed. These include offers of allegiance, statements by prominent figures, and Ali's own actions and words. This lesson walks through these evidences in order.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of evidences
Al-Razi lists several historical events. Read through each one and note how each points to the absence of a clear designation.
He uses examples like the offer of allegiance by al-Abbas, Umar's offer, and Ali's own statements.
2
Examine the significance of al-Abbas's offer
Al-Abbas offered to pledge allegiance to Ali to prevent dispute, implying that no prior text existed.
3
Consider statements of other companions
Umar offered allegiance to Abu Ubayda, and Abu Bakr suggested Umar or Abu Ubayda—showing they did not know of a designated successor.
Also note Abu Bakr's wish that he had asked the Prophet.
4
Analyze Ali's own actions
Ali accepted the shura council, offered allegiance to Talha, and argued based on general bay'a, not nass. He also apologized for delaying his pledge.
These actions contradict the claim that he had been explicitly designated.
5
Conclude with other evidence
Zayd ibn Ali and other Ahl al-Bayt figures denied the existence of such a text, and the companions consistently called Abu Bakr 'Caliph of the Messenger of God'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الرازي: ومن العجائب أن الكاملين من علماء الشيعة لم يبلغوا كل عصر حد الكثرة فضلاً عن التواتر وأن عوامهم وأوساطهم لا يقدرون أن يفهموا كيفية هذه الدعوى على الوجه المحقق، وأن غلاتهم زعموا أن المسلمين ارتدوا بعد النبي ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) ولم يبق على الإسلام إلا عدد يسير أقل من العشرة ، فكيف يدعون التواتر في ذلك الطريق . الثاني - روايات وأمارات ربما تفيد باجتماعها القطع بعدم النص، وهي كثيرة جداً كقول العباس لعلي : امدد يدك أبايعك . تقول الناس : هذا رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) بايع ابن عمه فلا يختلف عليك اثنان. وقول عمر لأبي عبيدة (رضي الله تعالى عنه) : امدد يدك أبايعك. وقول أبي بكر : بايعوا عمر أو أبا عبيدة. وقوله : وددت أني سألت النبي ( ) عن هذا الأمر فيمن هو ، وكنا لا ننازعه وكدخول علي رضي الله تعالى عنه في الشورى، فإنه رضي بإمامة أيهم كان. وكقوله (رضي الله تعالى عنه) لطلحة (رضي الله تعالى عنه : إن أردت بايعتك وكاحتجاجه على معاوية ببيعة الناس له، لا بنص من النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وكقوله حين دعي إلى البيعة : اتركوني والتمسوا غيري، وكمعاضدته أبا بكر وعمر والإشارة عليهما بما هو أصلح حين خرج أبو بكر لقتال العرب وعمر لقتال فارس وكعدم تعرضه لذلك النص في شيء من خطبه ورسائله ومفاخراته ومخاصماته، وعند تأخره عن البيعة، وكإنكار زيد بن علي مع علو رتبته هذا النص، وكذا كثير من سادات أهل البيت. وكتسمية الصحابة أبا بكر مدة حياته بخليفة رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم ) .
Al-Imam al-Razi said: Among the wonders is that the perfect ones among the Shi'a scholars have not reached in every age the limit of multitude, let alone tawatur (mass transmission), and their common people and middle ones are not able to understand how this claim is in a verified manner, and their extremists claimed that the Muslims apostatized after the Prophet (peace be upon him) and there remained upon Islam only a number less than ten, so how do they claim tawatur in that path? Second: Narrations and indications that perhaps together yield certainty of the absence of nass (explicit text), and they are very many, like the statement of al-Abbas to Ali: Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you. The people would say: This is the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) pledging allegiance to his cousin, so two would not differ over you. And the statement of Umar to Abu Ubayda (may God be pleased with him): Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you. And the statement of Abu Bakr: Pledge allegiance to Umar or Abu Ubayda. And his statement: I wish that I had asked the Prophet ( ) about this matter as to whom it belongs, and we would not dispute him. And Ali's (may God be pleased with him) entry into the shura (consultation council), for he was pleased with the imamate of whichever of them it was. And his statement (may God be pleased with him) to Talha (may God be pleased with him): If you wish, I will pledge allegiance to you. And his argument against Muawiya by the people's pledge to him, not by a text from the Prophet (peace be upon him). And his statement when summoned to the pledge: Leave me and seek someone else. And his support of Abu Bakr and Umar and his advice to them in what was more beneficial when Abu Bakr went out to fight the Arabs and Umar to fight Persia. And his not mentioning that text in any of his sermons, letters, boasts, or disputes, and at his delay of the pledge. And Zayd ibn Ali's denial, despite his high rank, of this text, and likewise many of the nobles of the Ahl al-Bayt. And the companions' naming of Abu Bakr throughout his life as the Caliph of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a claim of an explicit text (nass) designating Ali as the Prophet's successor. It begins by quoting al-Razi, who points out the improbability of tawatur for such a claim, given the small number of knowledgeable Shi'a and the extremist view that most companions apostatized, which would undermine tawatur. Then it presents the second type of evidence: numerous historical narrations and indications that together yield certainty of the absence of nass. These include al-Abbas offering to pledge allegiance to Ali to prevent disagreement, Umar's offer to Abu Ubayda, Abu Bakr's suggestion of Umar or Abu Ubayda, Ali's own statements and actions such as entering the shura council, offering allegiance to Talha, arguing with Muawiya based on general bay'a rather than nass, and even apologizing for delaying his own pledge. Additionally, Zayd ibn Ali and many other Ahl al-Bayt figures denied the existence of such a text, and the companions consistently called Abu Bakr the 'Caliph of the Messenger of God', all of which contradict the notion of an explicit designation.

Key Terms
الشورى
البيعة
أهل البيت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Shi'a claim of an explicit text is supported by historical consensus.
Correction: Al-Razi provides numerous historical evidences from the actions and words of the Prophet's companions, including Ali himself, that collectively indicate there was no explicit text.

Checkpoint
What did Ali say when called to the pledge according to the passage?

B) 'Leave me and seek someone else.'

D) 'The Prophet appointed me.'

Key Takeaway
The collected historical evidences from the early Muslim community, including Ali's own actions, strongly indicate that there was no explicit text designating Ali as the Prophet's successor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage shows that the early community, including Ali, acted as if there was no explicit text for succession. Does that unsettle your assumptions about how divine guidance works? Can you trust a God who leaves such a critical matter to human consultation?
?
Imagine you were one of the companions who had to choose a leader without a clear divine directive. Would your faith waver in the face of such ambiguity? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on God's wisdom vs your need for explicit instructions?
?
You have just read that Zayd ibn Ali and many of the Ahl al-Bayt denied the existence of a text. If your own family members held a position contrary to what some claim, would you have the courage to side with them? Are you willing to follow truth even when it contradicts emotionally appealing narratives?

Sunni Proofs for the Caliphate of Abu Bakr
Sunni proofs for Abu Bakr's imamate with refutation of Shi'a views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main Sunni arguments for the caliphate of Abu Bakr, including consensus, Ali's actions, and textual evidence from the Qur'an and hadith.

Core Idea
Sunni evidence for Abu Bakr's caliphate combines communal consensus, Ali's own compliance, and prophetic texts.

This passage presents the key Sunni proofs establishing Abu Bakr as the first caliph after the Prophet. The author addresses both rational and textual arguments, while also refuting the Shi'a claim of taqiyya. As you read, notice how the evidence ranges from the consensus of the community to specific hadiths and a Qur'anic verse.

Guided Path
1
Overview of the argument
Read the passage to get the overall structure: it begins with a claim, then lists several proofs: consensus, Ali's compliance, the three-candidate argument, refutation of taqiyya, and textual evidence.
The passage is a compact list of proofs.
2
Examine the consensus evidence
Notice how the author uses the consensus of ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd (those who loosen and bind) and addresses that some hesitated initially. This shows that consensus is not invalidated by initial delay.
Consensus is a key Sunni source.
3
Consider Ali's role
Ali's compliance with Abu Bakr's orders, leading prayers, calling him caliph, and apologizing for his delayed pledge are used as proof that Ali himself recognized Abu Bakr's authority.
This counters Shi'a claims that Ali was the rightful caliph.
4
Review the textual proofs and refutation
Look at the Qur'anic verse (48:16) interpreted as referring to Abu Bakr, and the hadiths about following Abu Bakr and Umar, the thirty-year caliphate, and the pen-and-paper incident. Also note the refutation of taqiyya as deception.
Textual evidence supplements rational arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الخامس - الإمام (بعد رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أبو بكر رضي الله عنه) . وقالت الشيعة : علي . لنا إجماع أهل الحل والعقد وإن كان من البعض بعض توقف، وقد ثبت انقياد علي لأوامره ونواهيه و إقامة الجمعة والأعياد معه وتسميته خليفة، والثناء عليه حياً وميتاً والاعتذار عن التأخر في البيعة، وأيضاً اتفقوا على أن الإمام أبو بكر، أو علي، أو العباس . ثم أنهما لن ينازعاه فتعين . وحديث التقية تضليل للأمة. ولو كانت ، لكانت في زمن معاوية، وقد يتمسك بقوله تعالى: قل للمخلفين من الأعراب . . (٢) الآية . فالداعي المفترض الطاعة أبو بكر عند المفسرين، وعمر عند البعض، وفيه المطلوب. وبقوله ( ) : اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر (٣) وقوله ( ) : الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة (٤) وقوله ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) في مرضه : ائتوني بكتاب وقرطاس أكتب
He said: The fifth section – The Imam (after the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) is Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him). And the Shi'a said: Ali. For us is the consensus of the people of solution and contract, although there was some hesitation from some, and it is established that Ali submitted to his orders and prohibitions, and established Friday and Eid prayers with him, and called him caliph, and praised him alive and dead, and apologized for the delay in the pledge. Also, they agreed that the Imam is Abu Bakr, or Ali, or al-Abbas. Then the two would not dispute him, so he was determined. And the hadith of taqiyya is a deception of the ummah. If it were, it would be in the time of Muawiya. And one may adhere to His statement, the Exalted: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Arabs...' (2) the verse. So the caller who must be obeyed is Abu Bakr according to the exegetes, and Umar according to some, and in that is what is sought. And by his statement ( ): 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and Umar' (3), and his statement ( ): 'The caliphate after me is thirty years' (4), and his statement (peace be upon him) in his illness: 'Bring me a book and a scroll so that I may write...'
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is the fifth section of the discussion, affirming that the Imam after the Prophet is Abu Bakr. The Sunni evidence includes: 1) Consensus of the people of solution and contract (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd), even if some hesitated initially. 2) Ali's own compliance with Abu Bakr's commands, performing prayers with him, calling him caliph, praising him, and apologizing for his delay in giving the pledge—proving that Ali recognized his caliphate. 3) The agreement that the Imam is one of three: Abu Bakr, Ali, or al-Abbas, and since the other two did not contest him, Abu Bakr was determined. 4) Refutation of the Shi'a claim of taqiyya (dissimulation) as deception; if taqiyya were justified, it would be in the time of Muawiya, not earlier. 5) Qur'anic verse (48:16) interpreted by many exegetes as referring to Abu Bakr as the caller to jihad who must be obeyed, or Umar according to some. 6) Hadiths: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar', 'The caliphate after me is thirty years', and the incident of pen and paper during the Prophet's illness.

Correction: The passage shows that Sunni proofs include not only consensus but also Ali's compliance, a rational argument from the three candidates, and explicit textual evidence from the Qur'an and hadith.

?

The Prophet's Silence on Successor Was Not Negligence
Refutes the objection that the Prophet's silence on a successor was negligence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's not explicitly naming a successor was not negligence but a deliberate delegation to the community's leaders.

Core Idea
Leaving explicit designation was not neglect—it was trust in communal wisdom.

This passage answers a critical objection: if the Prophet left no explicit successor, does that mean he neglected that duty? The author argues that such a conclusion is false because the Prophet, who clarified lesser matters, would not ignore this great one. Instead, he subtly guided the community to choose the most suitable leader.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage closely
Read the Arabic passage once for gist, then read the translation. Note the two distinct answers given.
The passage begins with 'والجواب' signaling the response.
2
Identify the two arguments
The first argument: the Prophet would not neglect a great matter when he clarified lesser ones. The second: the silence was delegation to the people of understanding and leaders.
Look for the repetition of 'والجواب' which marks the second argument.
3
Reflect on the concept of delegation
The text says the Prophet entrusted the choice to 'أهل الحل والعقد' with subtle hints. Consider why this is not negligence but a sign of wisdom.
This connects to the broader Sunni doctrine of collective ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب أن ترك التنصيص على معين ليس إهمالاً) من النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أن يهمل مثل هذا الأمر الجليل، وقد بين ما هو بالنسبة إليه أقل من القليل. والجواب أن ترك النص الجلي على واحد بالتعيين ليس إهمالاً بل تفويض معرفة الأحق الأليق إلى آراء أولي الألباب، واختيار أهل الحل والعقد من الأصحاب، وأنظار ذوي البصيرة بمصالح الأمور ، وتدبير سياسة الجمهور، مع التنبيه على ذلك بخفيف الإشارة، أو لطيف العبارة نوع بيان لا يخفى حسنه على أهل العرفان.
And the answer: That leaving explicit designation of a specific person is not negligence from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he would neglect such a great matter, while he has clarified what is, relative to it, less than little. And the answer: That leaving explicit text on one person by designation is not negligence, but rather delegation of knowledge of the more rightful and suitable to the opinions of people of understanding, and the choice of the people of loosening and binding from the companions, and the views of those possessing insight into the interests of affairs and the management of the polity of the public, with alerting to that by a subtle indication or a refined expression of a type of explanation whose goodness is not hidden from people of gnosis.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an objection: why didn't the Prophet explicitly name a successor? The author argues that the failure to do so was not negligence because the Prophet never neglects important matters. Rather, it was a deliberate delegation to the community, specifically the people of resolution and contract (أهل الحل والعقد), to choose the most suitable leader. The Prophet provided subtle indications rather than explicit texts, which are clear to people of discernment.

Key Terms
التنصيص
ترك
الإهمال
أولي الألباب
أهل الحل والعقد
البصيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's silence means he inadvertently forgot or neglected to name a successor.
Correction: The text clarifies that the silence was deliberate: it was a delegation to the community's leadership with subtle indications, not negligence.

Checkpoint

A) He forgot to do so.
B) He delegated the decision to the people of resolution and contract.
C) He was prevented by his illness.
D) He intended to do so later but died.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's silence on a successor was not negligence but a wise delegation to the community's leadership to choose the most suitable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you recall a situation where someone's silence on an important matter led you to doubt their care? How does this lesson challenge your automatic assumption that silence equals neglect, and will you train yourself to consider the possibility that they deliberately entrusted responsibility to others?
?

?
The Prophet delegated the choice of caliph to 'people of understanding' and 'people of loosening and binding'. In your own community, who are those people? Are you among them, or do you actively support them? How will you take concrete steps to ensure that decisions in your spheres of influence are made by those with sound understanding, not by mere popularity or power?

Proofs for Abu Bakr's Caliphate
Enumerates multiple proofs for Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the cumulative case for Abu Bakr's caliphate based on consensus, textual proofs, and practical precedent.

Core Idea
Multiple probable evidences together yield certainty in the caliphate of Abu Bakr.

This passage presents a series of arguments used by Sunni scholars to establish Abu Bakr as the first caliph. Starting with the claim and the Shia opposition, the author lists several categories of evidence: consensus, Ali's actions, Quranic interpretation, prophetic hadiths, and practical precedents like leading prayer. These individually probable proofs collectively produce certainty, though the author notes the matter is subsidiary and probability suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and counterclaim
Notice the opening: 'The Imam after the Messenger is Abu Bakr.' The Shia said Ali. This establishes the sectarian context.
2
Examine the first evidence: consensus and Ali's submission
The author cites the consensus of the people of loosening and binding, and then shows that Ali himself submitted to Abu Bakr's authority.
3
Analyze the textual proofs from Quran and Hadith
Several hadiths and a Quranic verse are quoted as direct evidence. Note how each is interpreted to support Abu Bakr.
4
Consider the practical proofs: prayer leadership and community acceptance
The Prophet appointing Abu Bakr to lead prayer is a powerful symbol, and the community's acceptance is cited as proof.
5
Understand the cumulative argument
The author concludes that these are probable evidences that together yield certainty, and because it is a subsidiary matter, probability is enough.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الخامس - الإمام (بعد رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أبو بكر رضي الله عنه) . وقالت الشيعة : علي . لنا إجماع أهل الحل والعقد وإن كان من البعض بعض توقف، وقد ثبت انقياد علي لأوامره ونواهيه و إقامة الجمعة والأعياد معه وتسميته خليفة، والثناء عليه حياً وميتاً والاعتذار عن التأخر في البيعة، وأيضاً اتفقوا على أن الإمام أبو بكر، أو علي، أو العباس . ثم أنهما لن ينازعاه فتعين . وحديث التقية تضليل للأمة. ولو كانت ، لكانت في زمن معاوية، وقد يتمسك بقوله تعالى: قل للمخلفين من الأعراب الآية . فالداعي المفترض الطاعة أبو بكر عند المفسرين، وعمر عند البعض، وفيه المطلوب. وبقوله: اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر . وقوله: الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة . وقوله ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) في مرضه : ائتوني بكتاب وقرطاس أكتب كتاباً لا يختلف فيه اثنان . ثم قال : يأبى الله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر، وبأن المهاجرين الذين وصفهم الله بأنهم الصادقون كانوا يخاطبونه بيا خليفة رسول الله ، وبأن النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) استخلفه في الصلاة ولم يعزله. ولذا قال علي (رضي الله عنه) : رضيك رسول الله لديننا فرضيناك لدنيانا. وبأنها لو لم تكن حقاً لما كانت جماعة رضوا بها وسكتوا عليها خير أمة أخرجت للناس يأمرون بالمعروف وينهون عن المنكر، وهذه ظنيات ربما تفيد باجتماعها القطع. مع أن المسألة فرعية يكفي فيها الظن .
He said: The fifth research — The Imam after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him). And the Shia said: Ali. We have the consensus of the people of loosening and binding, even if some had some hesitation. And it has been established that Ali submitted to his commands and prohibitions, conducted Friday prayers and holidays with him, called him caliph, praised him alive and dead, and apologized for his delay in allegiance. Also, they agreed that the Imam is either Abu Bakr, Ali, or al-Abbas. Then they will not dispute him, so he is determined. And the hadith of taqiyya is misguidance of the nation. And if it were, it would have been in the time of Muawiya. And he may hold on to His saying the Exalted: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins...' the verse. So the caller who must be obeyed is Abu Bakr according to the exegetes, and Umar according to some, and in it is what is sought. And by his saying: 'Follow those after me, Abu Bakr and Umar.' And his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years.' And his saying (peace be upon him) in his illness: 'Bring me a script and a sheet, I will write a book after which you will not differ.' Then he said: 'Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' And that the Muhajirun whom Allah described as the truthful used to address him as 'O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah.' And that the Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed him as imam in prayer and did not remove him. Hence Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'The Messenger of Allah approved you for our religion, so we approve you for our worldly affairs.' And that if it were not true, the community would not have accepted and remained silent upon it, the best nation brought forth for mankind, commanding good and forbidding evil. And these are probable evidences that might together yield certainty. Nevertheless, the matter is subsidiary, and probability is sufficient for it.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of multiple proofs for the caliphate of Abu Bakr as the first Imam after the Prophet. The author begins with the claim that the Imam is Abu Bakr, and the Shia say Ali. Then he lists evidences: 1) Consensus of the people of loosening and binding (أهل الحل والعقد), even if some hesitated. 2) Ali's submission to Abu Bakr's authority and his participation in public duties. 3) The fact that the possible candidates were limited to Abu Bakr, Ali, or al-Abbas, and the latter two did not dispute him. 4) Rejection of the Shia concept of taqiyya (dissimulation). 5) A Quranic verse (48:16) interpreted by exegetes as referring to Abu Bakr as the caller to be obeyed. 6) Hadiths: 'Follow those after me, Abu Bakr and Umar;' 'The caliphate after me is thirty years;' the incident of the pen and paper where the Prophet said 'Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' 7) The Muhajirun calling him caliph. 8) The Prophet appointing him to lead prayer. 9) Ali's saying. 10) The community's acceptance. The author notes these are probable evidences that together yield certainty, and since the matter is subsidiary, probability suffices.

أهل الحل والعقد
البيعة

الداعي المفترض الطاعة
الاستخلاف في الصلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shia position is based on explicit text from the Prophet designating Ali as his successor.
Correction: The author demonstrates that there are multiple proofs from the Prophet's words and actions, as well as consensus, that support Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
Which evidence does the text mention as indicating Abu Bakr's caliphate?
A) Ali's refusal to obey Abu Bakr.
B) The Prophet's statement 'Follow those after me, Abu Bakr and Umar.'
C) The Shia doctrine of taqiyya.
D) Ali's claim to be caliph.

Key Takeaway
The caliphate of Abu Bakr is supported by a cumulative body of probable evidences that together yield certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author argues that because the community accepted Abu Bakr—and they are the best nation—their acceptance is a proof. Think of a time when you strongly disagreed with a decision made by the Muslim community around you. Did you trust their collective wisdom, or did you insist on your own judgment? What would it take for you to submit like Ali did, even if you initially hesitated?
?
Ali praised Abu Bakr alive and dead and even apologized for delaying his allegiance. Is there someone in your life whom you have opposed or been slow to accept? Are you willing to genuinely praise them and apologize, even if you feel justified in your delay? What is holding you back?
?
The author dismisses taqiyya as misguidance. Are there areas of your faith where you have hidden your true beliefs to avoid conflict or criticism? How does this lesson challenge your own use of dissimulation in your daily interactions? What would it cost you to be completely honest about your convictions?

The Primary Proof: Consensus of the Community
Establishes doctrinal claim and presents consensus as main proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the primary proof for Abu Bakr's caliphate is the consensus of the people of loosening and binding, and that the Sunni stance distinguishes from Shia and Rawandiyya.

Core Idea
Consensus of the community is the decisive evidence for rightful leadership.

This lesson presents the foundational claim about the caliphate after the Prophet. It establishes the Sunni position alongside the Mu'tazila, distinguishes from Shia and the Rawandiyya sect, and introduces the main argument: the consensus of the qualified electors.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify groups
Read the passage and note the different groups mentioned: Sunnis, Mu'tazila, Shia, Rawandiyya. Understand their positions on the caliphate.
The text states 'according to us and the Mu'tazila and most sects, Abu Bakr'.
2
Spot the primary proof
Identify the main proof presented for Abu Bakr's caliphate. The text says 'the first — and it is the main proof — the consensus of the people of loosening and binding'.
3
Consider initial hesitation
Notice that the passage acknowledges some hesitation from the Ansar and Abu Sufyan. This shows that consensus was not immediate but was eventually reached.
The examples given illustrate that there was some initial opposition.
4
Reflect on the role of consensus
Think about why consensus is considered a decisive proof in Sunni theology, even when there is some delay or discussion.
Consensus represents the collective agreement of the qualified scholars and leaders.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحق بعد رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) عندنا وعند المعتزلة وأكثر الفرق أبو بكر . وعند الشيعة علي رضي الله تعالى عنه . ولا عبرة بقول الروندية أتباع القاسم بن روند إنه العباس (رضي الله تعالى عنه). لنا وجوه : الأول - وهو العمدة، إجماع أهل الحل والعقد على ذلك. وإن كان من البعض بعض تردد وتوقف على ما روي أن الأنصار قالوا منا أمير ومنكم أمير. وأن أبا سفيان قال : أرضيتم يا عبد مناف أن يلي عليكم تيم؟ والله لأملأن الوادي خيلاً ورجلاً. وذكر في صحيح البخاري وغيره من الكتب الصحيحة أن بيعة علي وقع في هذا الموضع من المصنف بياض مقدار ما يسع فيه كلمتان) وفي إرسال أبي بكر وعمر أبا عبيدة بن الجراح إلى علي رضي الله عنه رسالة لطيفة من رواها الثقات بإسناد صحيح تشتمل على كلام كثير من الجانبين، وقليل غلظة عمر و علي ، أن علياً جاء إليهما ودخل فيما دخلت فيه الجماعة ، وقال حين قام عن المجلس : بارك الله فيما ساءني وسركم، فيما روي أنه لما بويع لأبي بكر (رضي الله تعالى عنه وتخلف علي والزبير والمقداد، وسلمان، وأبو ذر، أرسل أبو بكر من الغد إلى علي فأتاه مع أصحابه، فقال: ما خلفك يا علي
The truth after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), according to us and the Mu'tazila and most sects, is Abu Bakr. And according to the Shia, Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). And no consideration is given to the saying of the Rawandiyya, followers of al-Qasim ibn Rawand, that it is al-Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him). We have proofs: The first — and it is the main proof — the consensus of the people of loosening and binding upon that. Even if some had some hesitation and delay, as it is narrated that the Ansar said: 'An emir from us and an emir from you.' And that Abu Sufyan said: 'Are you content, O Banu Abd Manaf, that a man from Taym should rule over you? By Allah, I will fill the valley with horses and men.' And it is mentioned in Sahih al-Bukhari and other authentic books that the pledge to Ali (here there is a blank in the text of the author to the extent of two words) And in the sending of Abu Bakr and Umar with Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), a subtle message narrated by trustworthy narrators with a sound chain, containing much speech from both sides, and a little of Umar's harshness and Ali's, that Ali came to them and entered into what the community had entered into, and said when he stood up from the gathering: 'May Allah bless what grieved me and pleased you.' According to what is narrated that when the pledge was given to Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), and Ali, al-Zubayr, al-Miqdad, Salman, and Abu Dharr held back, Abu Bakr sent the next day to Ali, and he came with his companions, and said: 'What kept you, O Ali?'

Commentary
This passage asserts the correct position among Sunnis, Mu'tazila, and most sects that Abu Bakr is the rightful caliph after the Prophet, while the Shia hold Ali. It dismisses the Rafida (Rawandiyya) who claim al-Abbas. Then the author presents the main proof: consensus of the people of loosening and binding. He acknowledges some initial hesitation, as reported from the Ansar and Abu Sufyan. He references Sahih al-Bukhari regarding Ali's pledge. A blank in the text is noted. He then recounts a subtle message sent to Ali via Abu Ubayda, which led Ali to join the consensus. The story concludes with Abu Bakr asking Ali why he delayed.

Historical Confirmation: Ali's Pledge to Abu Bakr
Narrates historical events confirming Ali's pledge to Abu Bakr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus for Abu Bakr was confirmed through the actions of Ali and other companions, as recorded in reliable sources.

Core Idea
Ali's eventual pledge demonstrates the universal acceptance of Abu Bakr's caliphate.

This lesson continues the discussion by examining the historical events that solidified the consensus. It references Sahih al-Bukhari and the narrative of Abu Bakr sending a delegation to Ali, leading to Ali's public acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Note the authoritative source
The passage references Sahih al-Bukhari and other authentic books regarding Ali's pledge. This grounds the narrative in reliable hadith literature.
There is a blank in the text indicating missing words.
2
Understand the delegation
Abu Bakr and Umar sent Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah to Ali with a message. This shows the caliph's effort to bring Ali into the consensus peacefully.
The message is described as 'subtle' containing speech from both sides.
3
Observe Ali's response
Ali came to them and entered into what the community had entered. He said: 'May Allah bless what grieved me and pleased you.' This indicates his acceptance despite earlier reluctance.
The narrative includes some details of Umar's harshness and Ali's response.
4
See the final outcome
When Abu Bakr sent for Ali after the pledge, Ali came with his companions and was asked why he had delayed. This shows that he eventually joined the consensus.
